Important News

Honjo Sends Itagaki to Persuade Ma Zhanshan

Ma Zhanshan's Attitude is Firm

Itagaki Returns Without Success

Harbin Correspondence, on the 6th of this month, Itagaki, the Chief of Staff of the Japanese Kwantung Army Command, on the orders of Honjo Shigeru, came to Harbin from Shenyang. Those traveling with him included Fukushima, a translator from the Kwantung Army, accountant Sometomiya, and reporters from British and German newspapers, a total of five people. They stayed at the North Manchuria Hotel in Daoli. At noon, they went to see Zhang Jinghui for a very secret consultation. After 1:00 PM, Itagaki took a plane to Heihe. Returning to Harbin at about 3:00 PM, the Japanese troops on the Qiqihar line had already advanced to the Tahaer and Yangguantun areas. Due to Itagaki's arrival, they all stopped in the local area and no longer advanced. The situation on the Qiqihar line suddenly eased. That evening, Itagaki went to Zhang Jinghui's private residence and invited Zhao Zhongren, a Chinese traitor from Heihe Province, to come. The three parties talked for a long time. At about 8:00 PM, Zhang Jinghui, at the request of Itagaki, spoke to Ma Zhanshan on a long-distance call. Zhang said that the representative of the Japanese Kwantung Army will go to Hailun to meet with Xiufang (Ma's courtesy name), and will go tomorrow. Please send someone to receive them. Ma said that he did not need to negotiate directly with the Japanese, and the soldiers and people of Heihe Province were full of energy. Please do not come, otherwise accidents may happen, and he will not be responsible. Itagaki put his ear to the receiver and wanted to talk to Ma directly, but Ma did not answer and hung up the phone. At about 8:00 AM on the 7th, Itagaki, along with translator Fukushima and consulate staff Okado and Sugiyama, went to Ma's pier in Songpu. Accompanied by Zhao Zhongren and Han Shoupeng (former secretary of the Heihe Provincial Government), they first called Hailun from Ma's pier, requesting Ma Zhanshan to allow Itagaki to meet him at all costs. Ma unwillingly ordered a railcar to be called on the Hulan-Hailun line, and invited reporters from Chinese newspapers in Harbin to go with them. The meeting was scheduled for 2:00 PM at the Suihua station on the Hulan-Hailun line (117 kilometers from Harbin). At 1:55 PM, the special car carrying Itagaki arrived in Suihua. He then received a call from Hailun, stating that Suihua was inconvenient and that the meeting would be held in Hailun. Zhao Zhongren, Han Shoupeng, and the reporters took a car first. At 4:30 PM, Itagaki's car departed. Arriving in Hailun at 8:00 PM that night, an aide-de-camp from the Joint Military-Political Office escorted them to stay at Guangxin. Chinese and foreign reporters stayed at the Yitaiyong Trading Company. At 9:00 PM that night, Ma sent Chief of Staff Xie Ke to meet with Itagaki first and inquire about his intentions. Itagaki explained that he represented Commander Honjo and wanted to meet with Chairman Ma for a face-to-face talk. At 12:00 PM, Ma, along with Zhao Zhongren, Han Shoupeng, Xie Ke, and two translators, met at the Joint Military-Political Office in Guangxin. After meeting, Itagaki first said, "I represent Commander Honjo and have come to see Your Excellency for several matters to discuss." While speaking, he took out Honjo's business card from his sleeve (on which were written the characters "Please convey my regards to Chairman Ma"). He said that Commander Honjo ordered him to ask Your Excellency three questions: First, what is Your Excellency's current attitude and will you continue to resist the Japanese army to the end? Please answer clearly. Second, the conflict between the Heihe army and the Japanese army this time was a temporary misunderstanding. Can military actions be stopped in the future and can there be mutual understanding? Third, what are Your Excellency's thoughts on the previous battles? What the Japanese side now requests from Your Excellency is: (1) to preserve the peace of East Asia, so that no more wars will occur between China and Japan; (2) that China and Japan can thoroughly cooperate in businesses such as maintaining the security of the Northeast. The Kwantung Army respects Your Excellency's intentions and hopes to end the anti-Japanese actions and fully understand the Kwantung Army's true intentions. If military actions are stopped immediately, then Your Excellency can still be responsible for the military power of Heihe Province and mutually safeguard the peace of East Asia, because the Kwantung Army will never allow anti-Japanese actions to continue to exist in the Northeast. There is a complete plan and great determination to completely transform the future. As for the Hulan and Qiqihar lines, because of admiration for Your Excellency's bravery, the military plan will not be implemented immediately," etc. Ma replied, "Your representative's first request is what I have always prayed for, and the second item can also be agreed upon, but Chinese sovereignty must be respected, and there must be sincere goodwill. The military actions taken by the Heilongjiang army this time were purely for self-defense. I was appointed by the central government and do not know anything else. I hope that all disputes between China and Japan will be resolved as soon as possible, which is my deep wish. As for the actions of our army and our future attitude, your side should already be clear about it, so there is no need to state it again. In short, if the Japanese army does not oppress us, we will not attack." That night, during the conversation between the two parties, Itagaki constantly tempted Ma with benefits, forcefully arguing how strong the Japanese army was and how isolated the Heihe army was, and that resistance was useless, repeatedly pestering him until 2:35 AM on the 8th before bidding farewell and leaving. At 11:00 AM on the 8th, Itagaki visited Ma again, requesting Ma to go to Harbin to talk with Zhang Jinghui, and promising Ma to be the military and political assistant of Heilongjiang, with Zhang Jinghui serving as the chairman. If Ma was willing to agree, the Japanese army would withdraw from the Qiqihar line and no longer pressure him. Ma said that he did not object to Zhang Jinghui being the chairman of Heilongjiang, as they are both Chinese. However, he was appointed by the central government and could not secretly hand over the position. Harbin and Hailun are not far apart, and they can often discuss matters by telephone and do not need to go in person. The public sentiment in Hailun is extremely激昂, and it is best that representatives of your country do not come again in the future. Seeing that Ma's attitude was firm, Itagaki returned to Harbin today, dejected. It is heard that he is scheduled to return to Shenyang tonight to report back. (9th)

U.S. Embassy Releases Stimson's Remarks on the Manchurian Issue

Endorsing the Principles Contained in the League of Nations Resolution

Still Concerned About All Future Developments in This Matter

Reuters, Peiping, 12th. The U.S. Embassy received the declaration made by U.S. Secretary of State Stimson to the press on December 10 regarding the Sino-Japanese dispute in Manchuria. The translation is as follows: "The U.S. Government is very pleased that the Council of the League of Nations unanimously passed the resolution of December 10. This is a definite step in the long and difficult negotiation process carried out by Briand and his colleagues with great perseverance. The Council of the League of Nations convened on September 18, just as the Manchurian Incident occurred. China immediately invoked Article 11 of the League Covenant to petition the Council. China and Japan both participated in the Council's discussions in accordance with their obligations as signatories to the Covenant. The U.S. Government has strived to cooperate with the Council from the beginning and has supported its efforts. Therefore, it has sent notes to the governments of China and Japan through diplomatic channels. The League of Nations' efforts to prevent major wars and seek a peaceful resolution of the Manchurian case are not only of concern to the American people, but the U.S. Government is also directly involved and obligated under the Kellogg-Briand Pact and the Nine-Power Treaty of February 6, 1922, both of which it co-signed with China and Japan. This resolution stipulates the immediate cessation of hostilities, reiterates Japan's solemn promise to withdraw its troops into the railway zone as soon as possible, and provides for the dispatch of a commission of five investigators to conduct on-site investigations and report to the Council of the League of Nations on any circumstances that disrupt peace and good understanding between China and Japan. The provision for a neutral commission is crucial and is an organized step towards a final and fair resolution of the complex Manchurian issue. It is a new era of enlightened methods for implementing reconciliation of this problem, as recognized by both China and Japan. The principles it contains exist in many treaties of amity signed by the United States and have occupied a prominent position in the world's constructive peace mechanisms in recent years. The work of this type of commission can reduce the heat of the dispute and allow for a careful study of the underlying issues. The final resolution of the Manchurian case must be achieved by China and Japan themselves through an agreement. What concerns the United States is that the methods used in this resolution should comply with the obligations of the treaties we have signed and should not endanger world peace. The result must not be obtained through the oppression of force. These are the principles advocated by the United States and the countries attending the Council of the League of Nations. However, the adoption of this resolution cannot be regarded as an endorsement of any actions taken in Manchuria to date. The U.S. Government, as a signatory to the Kellogg-Briand Pact and the Nine-Power Treaty, cannot deliberately ignore the events that have occurred. The future effectiveness of the resolution depends entirely on the good faith of both sides in fulfilling their promise to oppose further warfare and on the spirit of utilizing the various provisions to achieve a final resolution. In view of the obligations of the treaties it has signed, the U.S. Government will continue to be deeply concerned about all future developments in this matter."

Japanese Dissatisfaction with the Actions of the Warlords

Concerned that They Will Invite Suspicion from the Great Powers

But the Japanese Warlords Still Want to Go Their Own Way

The Greater America Evening News, Shenyang, 13th. Tsurumi, the son-in-law of the late Count Goto, is known for his familiarity with Japanese-American relations. After touring and lecturing in the United States for a year, he came to Liaoning to inspect the situation in the three eastern provinces. In a speech in Dalian, he discussed former U.S. Army Chief of Staff Pershing's criticism of the actions of the Japanese army in the Northeast, saying that the financial and economic recovery of the United States, Britain, and Germany and the completion of the Soviet Union's Five-Year Plan are not far off. Japan must immediately focus on eliminating the root causes of existing foreign misunderstandings. Mr. Tsurumi also recounted the history of U.S.-Japan relations since the Russo-Japanese War, saying that the Twenty-One Demands made by Japan to China in 1915 greatly damaged U.S.-Japan relations, and that the anti-foreign land law in California further deepened this damage. After the Washington Conference, U.S.-Japan relations improved, and the United States' fear of Japanese aggression against China was somewhat allayed, but this military action has increased American suspicion again, etc. This speech has attracted great attention from the Japanese community here, because the Japanese have also expressed their dissatisfaction with the arrogance of the military. Consul General Hayashi has also tried to organize a committee that can represent the greater interests of the Japanese community in the three eastern provinces and place the military in a secondary position in order to unify the goals and policies of the Japanese in Manchuria. Mr. Hayashi returned to Tokyo for several days and only returned to Shenyang this afternoon for this matter, but it is heard that the Japanese warlords do not approve of this plan. They issued a declaration here today, claiming that the Japanese army has its own plan to maintain the Open Door Policy and world investment in Manchuria and Mongolia.

Memorial Week of the National Government

Cai Yuanpei Speaks on the Mission of the Special Education Committee

The National Government held a memorial week for the late Premier Sun Yat-sen on the morning of the 14th. Chiang Kai-shek, Cai Yuanpei, Yu Youren, Zhu Peide, Shao Lizi, Ma Fuxiang, Li Shuhua, Chen Qicai, He Yaozu, Ru Yuli, Wei Daoming, Chen Shaokuan, Yu Feipeng, Zhu Luhe, and other staff members, totaling more than 400 people, attended. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek led the ceremony, followed by a report by Cai Yuanpei on the mission of the Special Education Committee. He briefly stated that educational administration is the responsibility of the Ministry of Education, but the Central Political Council believes that there are various special issues in education during this time of national crisis that require collective wisdom. Therefore, a special committee was established, and there is absolutely no infringement on the powers of the Ministry of Education. When talking about special issues in education during the national crisis, one thinks of the patriotic movement of students. The patriotic movement of students is most welcome, but if academic studies are sacrificed due to the patriotic movement, the loss is significant, and the harm is almost equal to the loss of territory. During the European War, Germany's finances were extremely exhausted, but schools were not closed because students are the lifeline of the country. Famous scholars in countries with conscription systems can be exempted from military service because academic studies are the reserve force of the military, and the resources of youth cannot be easily sacrificed. Germany has Krupp, who can make the country's ordnance the best in the world. France has Pasteur, who can make the brewing and silk industries particularly stable, greatly increasing national wealth. The United States has Edison, who can create countless sources of profit for the United States. Moreover, during times of national crisis, it is an opportunity to promote creation. Our country now needs inventors like Krupp, Pasteur, and Edison. With a seven-year illness, seeking artemisia for three years can still save our poverty and weakness. If we continue to procrastinate, it will be incurable. If young people engage in patriotic movements by giving speeches on the current situation during their spare time or expressing their opinions in writing, it will be beneficial and harmless. Now, young people emphasize strikes and marches, and some travel thousands of miles to the capital to protest, sacrificing time and studies. Among these tens of thousands of young people, there may be several inventors or a few great inventors like Pasteur and Edison. It is truly pitiful and regrettable that they sacrifice a lot of time and studies when they are young. Now, patriotic young people, motivated by patriotic enthusiasm, mistakenly believe that the original basic sciences are not a way to save the country. We now need to examine the school curriculum to see if there are any subjects that can be temporarily reduced and replaced with textbooks that are directly related to the national crisis. The most direct is naturally military training. This was originally requested by students in various places. Now, why are students in various places sacrificing the time to receive training and exchanging it for running around? Is it necessary to intensify the current military training? That is why we set up a military training group and asked military experts to study this issue. Secondly, the current situation, the comparison of the strengths of various countries, and the various preparations that should be made in terms of national defense, economy, and transportation all contain many issues. If experts give detailed lectures, it will not only boost morale but also be beneficial to the present and the future. That is why we set up a special lecture group, not only to consult with the existing teachers in various schools but also to invite famous scholars to give lectures in various places in turn. We set up a compilation and translation group to collect and organize materials for special lectures. We set up a general affairs group to take care of the patriotic activists who have arrived in Beijing, so as to reduce difficulties and avoid danger. The above groups are currently temporarily staffed by members appointed by the Political Conference, and specialized scholars will be invited to join them to gather wisdom and broaden ideas. If a national crisis conference is established in the future and there is a section on education, the work of this committee can be transferred, and the committee can be dissolved, etc." The meeting adjourned after the report.

The Northeast Authorities Transport Salt to Raise Funds

Establish a Jiyun Committee to Promote the Sales of Lu Salt

Peiping Correspondence. Since the September 18th Incident, troops from the Northeast have gathered in Guannei, and various civilian and military organizations in Shenyang have also moved to Peiping and Tianjin to continue their work as usual. However, the financial resources of the Northeast have long been cut off, and the provinces of Hebei and Jehol are even struggling to take care of themselves. As a result, the troops' salaries and the salaries of various organizations have been supported for months, and they are gradually feeling exhausted. Now that winter is approaching, the soldiers' cotton clothes and cold-weather equipment require a large amount of funds to cope with. Zhang Xueliang is facing great difficulties in this regard. He recently ordered the heads of the finance, salt affairs, and railway bureaus to discuss solutions. After discussion, it was decided to establish a Jiyun Committee to promote the sale of Lu salt in the Yu shore area and raise funds. Gao Jiyi has been appointed as the chairman of the committee, and Lu Muting, Jing Youyan, Zeng Guangxiang, and Jin Zaohua as members. The committee will be established soon, and the address will be located in the Political Affairs Committee. The provisional measures of the committee are as follows: (1) This committee organizes a special train to transport salt to promote the sales of Lu salt and raise funds quickly. (2) In order to encourage salt merchants to compete for transportation, those who report the transportation of salt to the Yu shore within one month from the date of announcement of these measures will be exempted from military donations (currently four yuan per bag). Those who exceed the time limit will pay as usual. (All procedures for salt merchants to report transportation will still be handled by the salt affairs agencies as usual, but after the audit agency issues the permit, the salt merchants shall report to the committee in writing or by telegram within 24 hours, and go to the transportation office to collect the transportation order for verification. (4) The committee accepts the aforementioned report, verifies that it is consistent with the transportation order, immediately registers it, and allocates vehicles for loading in the shortest possible time according to the order. When a train is full, it will be shipped immediately. (5) The railway freight and tax donations for the salt transported with the approval of the committee shall be handled in accordance with the regulations. (6) Salt that is exempt from military donations shall be limited to designated sales in the Yu shore area. (7) All salt transported to the Yu shore area must be delivered directly to the designated sales location, and there must be no scattering or backflow. (8) In addition to salt transported to the Yu shore area, salt merchants in other areas who report transportation within one month will be given priority transportation according to the order of reporting, but they shall not be exempt from donations. (9) When the salt transport vehicles return, they shall transport other urgently needed goods (such as food and fuel) within the scope of not delaying time, but they must be reported to the committee for approval in advance to prevent abuses. (10) If any personnel of the committee engage in corruption, they shall be dealt with in accordance with military law.

The Fujian Provincial Government Takes Over the Electric Power Company

All Members of the Anti-Japanese Association Resign

Fuzhou Correspondence. Regarding the opposition to the Electric Power Company and the private sale of Japanese goods by Zhengji Warehouse in Fuzhou, the joint meeting of the Party, government, and military at 2 pm on the 5th resulted in the following: (1) The Electric Power Company will be taken over by a committee organized by the Party, government, military, and business sectors. Gan Yun, a member of the Provincial Party Department, Chen Peikun, Xu Xianshi, Li Dingzhang, commander of martial law, Guo Yongrong, director of the Public Security Bureau, Guo Zeshou, president of the Bank of China, and Luo Mianhou, owner of Henghe Money Shop, were appointed as members on the spot. (2) The Japanese goods in Zhengji Warehouse will be temporarily sealed pending resolution. (3) Liu Chongwei, Liu Chonglun, Lin Tianmin, and Lin Xianmin were wanted and brought to justice. (4) Military and police agencies were ordered to strictly prohibit gatherings, parades, petitions, strikes, and work stoppages. Those who disobey the prohibition will be considered to be disrupting public order and will be detained and prosecuted. After the meeting adjourned, the provincial government issued a public notice to the public at 6 pm. On the 6th, stores and factories opened as usual, and the turmoil came to a halt for a while. At 2 pm on the 7th, the Electric Power Takeover Committee held its first meeting at the Provincial Government. It was decided to elect Xu Xianshi as the chairman of the committee. Xu Xianshi drafted the takeover procedures and measures. Chen Peikun and Gan Yun audited the company's income and expenditure accounts. Guo Zeshou and Luo Mianhou temporarily maintained the company's finances and informed the company's employees by letter to continue working and await further appointments. At the same time, the Anti-Japanese Association also held an emergency meeting and decided that all executive committee members would resign and submit their resignations to the provincial and county Party departments for the assignment of personnel to take over, and ordered all departments to complete the handover by the 8th. (December 8)

Fujian Finance Director He Gonggan Resigns

The Provincial Government Sends Personnel to Take Over the Department's Affairs

Fuzhou Correspondence. Finance Director He Gonggan, unable to cope with the demands from all parties, suddenly took the Huaan ship to Shanghai on the morning of the 6th. Before leaving, he cited the recurrence of his old illness as a reason and asked the provincial government for a two-week leave of absence, with the department's affairs being handled by the secretary-director, Du Luzhong. On the 7th, the provincial government sent Secretary Wu Xianzhang and Chen Weiyao, a member of the Anti-Smoking Committee (former secretary-director of the Finance Department), to the Finance Department to take over. It was found that most of the administrative expenses of the various agencies had only been paid until September, or a portion of October, and the department's bills that had not been paid exceeded 700,000 yuan. The provincial government now plans to clear the bills first and then raise funds to pay the administrative expenses. It has already consulted with Qianbang to mortgage 400,000 yuan from the tea industry business tax for the 21st year. However, Du Luzhong refused to act as an agent because the responsibility of the department's affairs was too great. Therefore, the provincial government plans to order the various secretaries and section chiefs to jointly take responsibility. As for the successor finance director, although there are rumors of many people, it is likely that a decision will be made after Yang Shuzhuang returns to Fujian. (December 9)

The Fujian Provincial Government Asks to Investigate the Fujian Opium Case

Denies Zheng Luosheng et al.'s Allegations That the Provincial Government Presided Over Opium Planting

Fuzhou Correspondence. The members of the provincial government, in response to the proposal by Zheng Luosheng et al., representatives of the Fourth Plenary Session, to investigate the opium planting case in Fujian, which claimed that the provincial government was presiding over the matter, held a symposium on the 8th. Yang Shuzhuang, Fang Shengtao, Zheng Baojing, Cheng Shiquan, Xu Xianshi, Chen Peikun, Lin Zhiyuan, Lin Jinan, and Ding Chaowu jointly proposed that the National Government promptly send officials to Fujian to thoroughly investigate in order to clarify the truth. It was decided to telegraph the Central Party Department, the National Government, the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Military Affairs, the Ministry of Interior, the Ministry of Finance, and the Anti-Smoking Committee in Nanjing on the 9th, saying, "Reading the newspaper, Zheng Luosheng et al. of the Fourth Plenary Session suggested that the opium planting case in Fujian be thoroughly investigated, saying that officials under the Party's rule openly plant opium and levy taxes, which is truly a break with the Party, the country, and humanity. Righteous and stern words, reading them makes one sweat. The original proposal also stated that opium seedlings in Fujian are most prominent in southern Fujian, and those in charge are the provincial government, and those who help them are the local military and political leaders, and even government officials personally go to supervise the levy, etc., blaming the provincial government, which is even more frightening. At the provincial government meeting on the Geng day, a report was submitted, and all members agreed that although the finances of the Fujian provincial government have been extremely difficult in recent years, it has never used the prohibition of opium to extort a penny from the people, which can be witnessed by heaven and earth. According to recent reports, various counties have resumed planting opium seedlings, which has been strictly prohibited by the provincial government's committee meeting. In accordance with Article 17 of the Anti-Smoking Law, officials who use their power to force others to commit the crime of planting opium shall be sentenced to death. Personnel from the Party, government, and military agencies were dispatched to supervise each other, and a report was submitted to the central government to order all units of the National Defense Army in the province to comply. In fact, it is still early in the season, and if the seedlings are eradicated, it can still be remedied. If the provincial government is negligent, it shall report the truth. As for saying that the provincial government itself presides over opium planting, it is not only a sinner of the Party and the country, but also a public enemy of the people. The names listed in the proposal are mostly Fujianese who are familiar with the facts. If they deliberately add fruit arrows to the provincial government, so that colleagues will wear this overturned pot, the facts are not consistent, and the situation is difficult to remain silent. Now that the Fourth Plenary Session has this proposal, we urgently request that it be thoroughly implemented in accordance with the case, and that officials be selected and sent to Fujian as soon as possible to conduct a strict investigation. If there is any destruction of the opium ban, regardless of military or political, they should be dealt with strictly according to the law and severely punished as a warning to the whole country. The telegram is urgent, and we hope that you will carefully consider it. The Fujian Provincial Government bows its head." (December 10)

Part of the Illegal Cases of Japan (4)

"On Managing Manchuria and Mongolia" written by Japanese national Shigeo Hosono: Mr. Shigeo Hosono, a Japanese national, published and distributed "On Managing Manchuria and Mongolia" in the spring of the 17th year [of the Republic of China, i.e., 1928]. Subsequently, a Chinese national, Wang Gongning, translated it into Chinese, titled it "The Japanese Annexation," and published it in Shanghai. Upon receiving the report, we immediately sent letters to our embassy in Japan, requesting them to purchase the original text and to negotiate the matter. Our embassy in Japan replied, stating that the book "On Managing Manchuria and Mongolia" had been read by officials upon its publication. Its wording was absurd, its claims barbaric and deeply reprehensible. They had pointed out the content to the Japanese authorities, requesting them to ban it. However, the Japanese authorities responded that such private writings were purely the expression of personal opinions, and unless they clearly violated laws or regulations, it was not easy to intervene with administrative actions. They also claimed that Hosono was unknown, and an investigation would only attract public attention, which would be like publishing advertisements for him. Despite repeated rebuttals, they maintained their position, and no concrete solution was reached.

The Case of the Japanese Warship "Tanikaze" Killing Fishermen in Pingtan: On the night of February 27th of the 17th year [of the Republic of China, i.e., 1928], the Japanese merchant ship "Kinjo Maru" ran aground and sank in the mist off Geligang, Pingtan, Fujian. Over thirty crew members and their luggage were rescued by a Chinese fishing boat owned by Li [omitted], and they boarded the Japanese warship "Aoi" to return to their country. The next day, when the Pingtan County Magistrate sent officials to investigate, the Japanese warship "Tanikaze" suddenly arrived and, without asking any questions, opened fire on the fishing boats and civilians on the shore, killing twelve people and injuring twenty-seven. In the afternoon, Japanese soldiers landed with weapons and searched houses one by one before leaving. The former Fujian Commissioner for Foreign Affairs lodged a serious protest with the Japanese Consul, declaring that all rights were reserved. The Japanese Consul replied that when the Japanese warship arrived, they saw many boats looting goods, and they opened fire to drive away the pirates, which was a measure that warships should take. The Commissioner refuted this by saying that most of the boats at the time were Chinese fishing boats. He asked what kind of goods they were allegedly looting and how they were doing so. He also pointed out that the fishing boats involved were among those that rescued the crew and their belongings, which was enough to prove that they were all honest fishing boats and not suspected of any crime. He added that the houses of the civilians on the shore were searched one by one afterward, and nothing was found, proving that there was no piracy. Therefore, the civilians who were victims in this incident were all innocent people. He demanded five things: punishment of the perpetrators, compensation to the families of the victims, indemnity, an apology, and a guarantee that this would not happen again. The Japanese Consul replied with a letter that still evaded responsibility and used the irrelevant excuse of pirates. The Commissioner reported the case to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in detail. After careful review, the Ministry found that the reasons given by the Japanese Consul did not match the facts and ordered the Commissioner to refute the Japanese Consul based on the reasons given. The Japanese Consul continued to distort the truth, rely on force, and engage in sophistry, and the case remained unresolved.

The Case of Damage in the Jinan Incident: On May 3rd of the 17th year [of the Republic of China, i.e., 1928], during the Jinan Incident, the casualties among Chinese soldiers and civilians and the loss of public and private property could not be investigated at the time because Jinan was occupied by Japanese military force. According to reports from various public and private sources, the statistics are as follows: (A) Regarding casualties, over 17,000 people died, over 3,000 people were injured, over 9,000 were either dead or injured (the original report did not distinguish between deaths and injuries), over 5,000 were captured, and over 280 were missing (disappeared). (B) Regarding property losses, (1) public property was valued at over 11.3 million yuan, and the value of items not yet valued was pending investigation and estimation. (2) Private property was valued at over 21.8 million yuan, and the value of items not yet valued was pending investigation and estimation. The above figures are based only on reports already received and statistically compiled. The total damage is probably several times greater than this. On March 28th of the 18th year [of the Republic of China, i.e., 1929], the Jinan Incident was resolved. Regarding the issue of damages, the protocol stated that each side would appoint an equal number of commissioners to establish a joint investigation committee to conduct on-site investigations and make decisions. At that time, it was agreed with the Japanese ambassador to appoint three commissioners each. The list of personnel appointed by our side was notified to the Japanese ambassador in June of that year. The Japanese side has not yet notified us of the appointment of an equal number of commissioners. A letter was sent again in May of the 19th year [of the Republic of China, i.e., 1930], but there was no response.

Japan Plans to Set Up Manchuria and Mongolia Pavilion at the Exposition: In September of the 17th year [of the Republic of China, i.e., 1928], an exposition was held in Nagoya. The city's news and communications [omitted] agency opened a major news conference and established a Manchuria and Mongolia Pavilion, placing it in the category of Japanese territories. This concerned the encroachment on China's sovereignty. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs cabled the Chinese ambassador in Japan to investigate and verify the facts and [omitted] protest. According to the reply, after careful investigation, the pavilion did exist. At the same time, the same situation existed in Kyoto. The ambassador protested to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, which said that it was only a display of exhibits and that there was no intention of regarding Manchuria and Mongolia as Japanese colonies. After repeated debates, they agreed to change the name to "Participation Pavilion." In March of the 19th year [of the Republic of China, i.e., 1930], the Executive Yuan ordered that attention be paid to the Japanese rewarding aggression towards Manchuria and Mongolia and that steps be taken to establish a Manchuria and Mongolia Pavilion in Tokyo this year. The Ministry cabled the Chinese Embassy in Japan on March 28th to investigate. According to the reply, inquiries were made to the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the Ministry of Commerce and Industry, and the Tokyo Metropolitan Government, and there were no plans to establish a Manchuria and Mongolia Pavilion in Tokyo. However, the Japan Industrial Association opened the Marine and Aviation Exposition in Ueno Park from March to May of this year. Inside the exhibition hall, there was an exhibit room of the South Manchuria Railway Company, displaying products from Dalian and Lushun, but there was no mention of "Manchuria and Mongolia." Furthermore, according to the embassy's cables on May 7th and 8th of the 19th year [of the Republic of China, i.e., 1930], the Matsuzakaya Department Store in Ueno, Tokyo, had a plan to establish a Manchuria and Mongolia Exposition. Contact was made with the business manager of the store, and he was persuaded to stop it. He said that the content of the exposition was purely commercial in nature and intended to attract trade, with absolutely no political implications, and he refused to stop it. However, he agreed to have the South Manchuria Railway Company take responsibility for it. A serious negotiation was held with the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and the Director of the Bureau stated that this kind of exhibition was only intended to introduce foreign affairs and had no political implications. He said that if China were to establish an exposition on Japanese affairs, Japan would certainly not object. After repeated arguments, he finally agreed to change it to an "Introduction to Manchuria and Mongolia Exposition" to be held on the sixth floor of the Matsuzakaya Department Store. It would display landscape photographs and product samples, and it would be a small-scale event with a duration of twenty days. Later, it was heard that Japan had listed Manchuria as a territory of Japan at the Antwerp Exposition. We cabled the Chinese embassy in Belgium to investigate, but no reply has been received.

The Case of Japanese Fishing Boats Trespassing into Chinese Territorial Waters to Fish: Starting from the 18th year [of the Republic of China, i.e., 1929], around one hundred Japanese fishing boats intruded into our fishing grounds from Longkou to Yangjiaogou. Other places, such as Ren Zhushan, Beidaihe, and Shidao and Shijiusuo in Shandong, also had Japanese ships intruding into the fishing nets. The losses amounted to over 30,000 yuan in one month. In June of that year, Japanese electric net boats trespassed into the area of Linqu County to fish, damaging the fishing gear of local fishermen, including over a dozen baskets of fishing hooks owned by Guan Yun and others, scattering the schools of fish and causing significant losses. From October to November, thirteen Japanese steamships fished in the waters off the Xinmin district. From the 18th to the 19th year [of the Republic of China, i.e., 1930], more than ten Japanese fishing vessels, such as the Hakata Maru, arbitrarily fished northeast of Huadao Mountain. In the spring of the 19th year [of the Republic of China, i.e., 1930], Japanese warships led over a thousand fishing boats, spreading them all over the waters outside Linhongkou and east of Mount Tai. On January 26th, a fishing boat operated by [omitted] was sunk by a Japanese ship in the Wenzhou area. The loss of the boat, fishing nets, and fishing gear was estimated at about 3,000 yuan. The loss of over 2,000 catties of fresh fish was estimated at about 600 yuan. From May to October, the Japanese ship "Hayabusa Maru" protected electric fishing boats and sailed near Furong Island in Laizhou Bay to fish. In September, Japanese fishing boats appeared in the Wusong, Yantai, and Baoshan areas. The submarine cables from Wusong to Yantai and from Baoshan to Yantai were repeatedly damaged by them. In October, the Japanese Penglai Fishing Company deployed fishing boats to fish deep into the coastal areas of Guangdong Province. In November, over twenty Japanese iron-hulled fishing boats intruded into the waters of Sheshan to fish. In January of the 20th year [of the Republic of China, i.e., 1931], nine Japanese electric boats loaded with guns sailed into Yulin Port and Yalong Port to fish. In February, over thirty Japanese fishing vessels, such as the Genmei Maru, Dalian Maru, and Man Sen Maru, fished in the waters of Jiangsu and Zhejiang. Our side stated that Japanese fishing vessels were intruding into Chinese territorial waters and fishing freely, tearing sails and destroying nets of Chinese fishing boats at will, and that Japanese warships patrolled the waters, prohibiting Chinese fishermen from fishing, even violently ramming fishing boats. This constituted an infringement on Chinese sovereignty. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs protested to the Japanese side, requesting them to order Japanese fishing boats not to fly the Chinese flag, not to arbitrarily intrude and fish wantonly, and to immediately withdraw from Chinese territorial waters and ports to avoid disputes. The Japanese side replied that Japanese fishing boats were all fishing in international waters and had never fished in Chinese territorial waters, and that no Chinese fishing boats had been persecuted by Japanese warships. The Japanese said that the dispatch of warships to maintain order was due to the danger of pirates, to provide protection for Japanese fishing boats, and to crack down on any improper behavior of these boats; there was no other intention. They claimed that there was no factual basis for the claim that Japanese warships were interfering with Chinese fishing boats. They further stated that if China were to send patrol ships, they would be willing to cooperate with Japan to reach a satisfactory solution. The Ministry [omitted] consulted with the relevant ministries and departments and made overall plans. To prevent clandestine vessels and crack down on Japanese fishing vessels using Chinese ports as bases for fishing, it was submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval to instruct customs to prohibit all steamships and engine-powered vessels under 100 tons engaged in trade between Chinese ports and overseas ports from February 1st of the 20th year [of the Republic of China, i.e., 1931]. Furthermore, all fish imported from foreign ports, except for those imported by bona fide merchant ships with bills of lading, would be prohibited from May 1st of the 20th year [of the Republic of China, i.e., 1931]. Subsequently, the Japanese side applied to the Customs Administration of the Ministry of Finance to have Japanese fishing boats excluded from the ban. The Customs Administration believed that the shipowners would be affected if they were suddenly banned, and agreed to order the customs to postpone the enforcement of the ban for three months to allow them to make other plans. Around April, the Japanese Chargé d'Affaires issued a note expressing objections to the above ban, requesting that necessary measures be adopted to allow Japanese fishing boats to continue fishing in the waters close to China's international waters. Our side refuted this based on reason. At the same time, the Japanese side requested that the ban be extended. The Ministry of Finance also approved a cable on April 27th stating that the Customs Administration reported that there would be difficulties in implementing the ban. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs immediately consulted with the Ministry of Industry and agreed to instruct the Customs by cable during the negotiation period to temporarily suspend the implementation of the ban. On June 20th, officials from the Ministries of Foreign Affairs, Industry, and Finance held a joint meeting and resolved that the issue of prohibiting Japanese fishing vessels from using Chinese seaports as bases would be handled by the diplomatic authorities who would negotiate with the Japanese Chargé d'Affaires, setting a deadline for withdrawal. If there were no results, the customs would enforce the ban.

The Case of Japanese Nationals Brutally Murdering Farmer Zhang Yutang in Gaiping County: After the owner of a morphine den, a Japanese national, was assassinated at the Gaiping Fenshui Railway Station, the Japanese police station dispatched officers to illegally arrest suspects within Chinese territory. The county magistrate repeatedly requested the Japanese police station to stop this practice. On May 23rd of the 18th year [of the Republic of China, i.e., 1929], three Japanese policemen arrested farmer Zhang Yutang in Bajiaoling, accusing him of being a suspect in the assassination of the morphine den owner. When they took him to the Japanese police station in Dashiqiao, the farmer, fearing for his life, tried to escape. The Japanese policemen fired their guns, injuring his thigh. The next day, the Japanese police station sent someone to ask the village chief to take him back for medical treatment, but to no avail. On the 25th, he died from his injuries. The village chief brought back his body and buried it. The Gaiping County Magistrate negotiated with the Japanese police station, demanding that the perpetrators be punished, that compensation be paid to the family of the victim, and that it be guaranteed that there would be no more arrests across borders in the future. At the same time, he reported the matter to the Yingkou Commissioner for Foreign Affairs for serious negotiation, but the case has not been resolved.

The Case of Japanese Police Breaking into the Liaoning Post Office and Stabbing a Postman: On June 15th of the 18th year [of the Republic of China, i.e., 1929], at 10:30 p.m., a Japanese policeman named Higure broke into the Liaoning Postal Administration Office in a rickshaw through the iron gate on the north side, passed through the office grounds, and went to the south gate. Finding the gate closed, he shouted loudly to have it opened. At this time, Li Wanlin, a mailman on duty in the gatehouse, and Zhen Zhankui, a postal assistant, heard the noise and came out. They politely tried to persuade him, saying that the gate was locked and that it would be best to go out through the north gate. The Japanese policeman was extremely unreasonable. As Li and Zhen escorted him to the entrance of the east building dormitory, the Japanese policeman suddenly drew his sword and slashed wildly, cutting Li's head and causing blood to flow profusely. Ignoring his injury, Li tried his best to hold on to the Japanese policeman. Seeing that his life was in danger, Zhen risked his life to step forward and snatch the Japanese policeman's weapon, running to a nearby branch office to report the incident. The branch office sent someone to take the Japanese policeman away. At the same time, the post office sent the injured mailman to the hospital for treatment. This case was submitted by the Liaoning Commissioner for Foreign Affairs to the local Japanese Consul General for negotiation, but no results have been obtained.

The Case of the Japanese Regiment Trampling and Destroying Farmland During Maneuvers in Changchun: The Japanese regiment stationed in Changchun often conducted field exercises, disregarding the farmers' production. In August of the 18th year [of the Republic of China, i.e., 1929], they trampled and destroyed nine mu of farmland owned by Li Sigong in Erdaogou. The former Changchun Commissioner for Foreign Affairs dispatched officials to investigate and estimate the losses together with the Japanese Consul and the military regiment, putting it at 120 Japanese yen. In other cases, the farmland of 16 households, including Lin Xiangchen in Huangguagou, was 6 xiang, the farmland of Hengyu, Zheng Ning, Rongxuan, and 4 other households was 12 xiang, and the sorghum field of Li Gongyi in Baizigou was 7 mu. The farmland of Gan Fengshu and 30 other households in Daping Village was over 150 xiang, with losses amounting to tens of thousands of yuan. Repeated letters were sent to the Japanese Consul, requesting him to investigate and demanding compensation for the losses. The Japanese Consul delayed in replying. In January of this year, the Japanese Consul sent a draft for 20 yuan, claiming that the damage to Li Sigong's farmland, which was 120 yuan, was excessive. He said that the Japanese military regiment had already directly negotiated with the victim, Li Sigong, and settled the matter with a draft for 20 yuan. He asked that it be passed on and claimed that Rong Ningxuan and others had not suffered any losses. The Commissioner refuted this by saying that the losses suffered by Li Sigong had been determined during the investigation and could not be settled with 20 Japanese yen. When he asked Li Sigong, he learned that the Japanese Consul's claim that he had negotiated with the Japanese regiment was completely false. The Japanese Consul, because the losses suffered by Li Sigong's household had already been jointly investigated and could not be denied, fabricated a story with 20 Japanese yen. The losses suffered by the other households, because the incident had occurred over a year ago and the traces had disappeared, were claimed to have not suffered any losses. The Commissioner immediately refuted this, but the Japanese Consul never replied.

The Case of Japanese Police Officer Injuring Mailman He Yousan in Liaoning: On August 23rd of the 18th year [of the Republic of China, i.e., 1929], when He Yousan, a mailman at the Liaoning Post Office, was delivering mail in the South Manchuria Railway-affiliated area, a Japanese policeman suddenly forcibly took him to the [omitted] Japanese police station, searched his mailbag, threw the letters on the ground, confiscated one copy of the [omitted] newspaper, and kicked and beat the mailman He Yousan. The Postmaster, Yan Ming, confirmed that there were injuries to his fingers and shins. He immediately separately met with the Japanese Consul, Nichide, and the Japanese Police Chief, Kanmu, and negotiated verbally, demanding that the offending policeman be punished. The Consul and the Police Chief both expressed regret and promised to investigate, but subsequently, the Japanese Consul General replied that the report received by the police station did not match the mailman's account and refused to comply. The Liaoning Postal Administration then transferred the entire case to the Liaoning Commissioner for Foreign Affairs for further handling. As of now, the Commissioner for Foreign Affairs has not reported any resolution to the case. (To be continued)

Local News

Songjiang

Provincial Order to Raise and Transport Engineering Expenses: The county government recently received a provincial order to raise and transport engineering expenses of 100,000 yuan in silver, to be cleared by the end of December. County Magistrate Shen, fearing that it would affect his promotion, personally received instructions from the Provincial Chairman, ordering him to do his utmost to urge collection and to ensure that the amount was fully paid by the deadline. However, the land price tax in the second district of the county has just been [omitted], and the collection is too slow to be of immediate help. In addition to notifying all business owners to expedite payment, it has been decided to borrow money first and report the payment. 40,000 yuan has already been borrowed in the first district, and the remaining five districts will jointly borrow 60,000 yuan at a monthly interest rate of 1.2%, using the second installment of the land price tax as collateral. Repayment will be made from the 21st of this month to the end of January. All districts have been ordered to borrow the full amount and report the payment before the 21st.

The Investigation into the Refugee Homicide: In the Mudflat of Fengjing Chao, there were many refugees picking firewood a few days ago, which led to a conflict with the villagers. A refugee named Tu Dongbin was beaten to death. After an investigation by the county court prosecutor's office, it was learned that the refugee leader, Wang Jingan, accused Zhang Xiaodi of being the murderer. It is now learned that both parties are negotiating a settlement out of court, but no agreement has been reached. The prosecutor's office summoned [omitted] witnesses today for questioning. Zhang Xiaodi confessed that the refugees started the conflict by picking firewood. The refugees' side claimed that they did not start the conflict. After hearing their statements about the out-of-court settlement, the magistrate ordered Zhang Xiaodi to be detained, and the others were told to wait for further instructions.

Wuxi

Youth Aid-to-Soldiers Corps Arrives in Wuxi with a Coffin: The Shanghai Youth Volunteer Corps to Aid Soldiers in the Northeast, which is fighting Japan, arrived in Wuxi from Suzhou by train at about 6 p.m. the night before. Upon hearing the news, seven organizations, including the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association of Wuxi, the County Chamber of Commerce, the Chamber of Commerce Corps, the Fire Brigade Federation, the Student Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, the Boy Scouts Society, and the Volunteer Corps, sent representatives to the station to welcome them. All 243 members of the corps got off the train, and were guided by the Boy Scouts Society to the General Labor Union to stay. The members wore different clothes, including plain clothes and military uniforms, and were full of energy. Their discipline was strict. There were three female members who also showed their strong spirit, which was admirable. They also carried a coffin for those who fell in the first battle. That evening, the seven organizations held a banquet at Yingbinlou to entertain the corps leader, Zhang Shaojie. The guests and hosts parted happily after 9 p.m. Yesterday morning at 11 a.m., people from all walks of life held a welcoming meeting in the park, followed by a parade throughout the city. They then went to the train station to take the train to Zhenjiang at 3 p.m.

Initiating a National Crisis Self-Salvation Association: Local Wuxi figures Fu Yiming and 102 others, in view of the daily national crisis, the failure of diplomacy, and the government's procrastination, initiated the organization of a National Crisis Self-Salvation Association based on the principle that everyone is responsible for their country. They issued a declaration and agreed on three things: (1) to supervise the government's diplomatic progress and to jointly resist any actions that harm the country's interests; (2) to promote the realization of democratic politics and to jointly resist any forces that harm society's interests and violate civil rights; and (3) anyone who is not a national criminal or a social pest is welcome to join and jointly save the country from its crisis. In recent days, many local gentry, celebrities, and young people have joined. A general meeting will be held in the coming days. An office will be set up in the first district office of the park [omitted].

Students in the Whole County Decide to Strike Again: At the previous fourth general meeting of the Wuxi Student Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, it was decided to continue attending classes as usual because the sacrifice of striking was too great. Yesterday, the fifth general meeting was held, chaired by Chen Shengqiao. It was decided (1) to reconsider the resolution of the previous meeting and to unanimously strike from today onwards because of the daily national crisis; (2) to schedule a meeting to continue on the 15th; (3) to send representatives from the Guozhuan and Furen schools to the Provincial Wuxi Middle School to explain everything and clear up misunderstandings.

Changzhou

Welcoming the Youth Aid-to-Soldiers Corps: Wujin's various agencies held a meeting at the County Party Headquarters on the 13th because the Youth Aid-to-Soldiers Corps will be passing through the area soon. They discussed welcoming methods and resolved: (1) to allocate 350 yuan for expenses, which will be borne by the various agencies; (2) to determine the County Party Headquarters, the County Farmers Association, and the Local Autonomy Research Association as accommodation locations; (3) to send a representative, Li Miaoshi, to Wuxi to coordinate; (4) to hold a welcoming meeting at the sports field; (5) to hold a demonstration parade at the time; and (6) to present a silk banner, two hot water bottles, and two dozen towels as gifts.

There Are Clues in the Finance Bureau Theft Case: More than 3,500 silver dollars were stolen from the iron safe in the cashier's office of the Wujin Finance Bureau. Bureau Chief Qian Zhaoda has now discovered that the cashier Luo Kuiqi has many problems with his accounts. He secretly deposited 10,000 yuan of tax money in the Da Lun Silk Store for interest. 300 silver dollars in cash were also found in his leather bag. Knowing that things were not good, Luo falsely claimed that he had taken sleeping pills and attempted suicide. He was sent to Wujin Hospital on the 13th. After gastric lavage, no poison was found. He was discharged from the hospital immediately. However, Luo is the nephew of Bureau Chief Qian. It is unknown how this will be handled.

Requesting Instructions on How to Clear Accumulated Arrears: County Magistrate Zhang of Wujin, with arrears totaling 78,600 taels of grain from past years and 52,800 shi of rice, plans to send one or two people from each district, along with grain police, to collect the arrears from door to door. All expenses will be covered by the fines for late payment of old arrears. He submitted ten measures to the provincial government on the 13th for review and implementation.

Zhenjiang

Yuyuan Money Shop Suspends Business: The Yuyuan Money Shop in Zhenjiang has been established for many years, with strong capital and a business turnover of about one million. It has had a surplus every year. This year, due to the impact of the flood in northern Jiangsu, it was difficult to recover loans, but deposits and interbank transactions had to be paid in full. With skillful management, it was still able to maintain operations. Recently, it was slightly affected by the constraint of a certain shareholder. Its cash flow suddenly became tight. Another shareholder tried to provide relief in the hopes of turning the crisis into an opportunity. However, Zhou Jiasan, the manager, believed that although the accounts receivable and payable could be offset, it was difficult to recover the loans and it was impossible to maintain operations. Therefore, he automatically announced the suspension of business. However, because the shareholders were not informed in advance and there were no corresponding measures taken afterward, it caused a lot of disputes. Depositors and various banks now intend to first clear the shop's accounts. If it can be maintained, they will discuss business operations with the shop's shareholders.

Nantong

The Dede in Hupu Burned Down: The Dede ship of the Shanghai-Yangzhou Dada Company set sail from Shanghai at 3:00 a.m. on the 13th. At about 11:00 a.m., it arrived at the Hupu River surface. Cotton in the cargo hold suddenly caught fire within ten days. The entire ship was engulfed in flames. After the ship caught fire, it sailed towards the beach. Passengers jumped into the river to escape. Fortunately, the Changsha and Jiangtan ships rescued them. More than 200 people were rescued. More than 200 people died. The ship has now turned into ashes.

A Refugee Boat Capsized in the Wind: On the morning of the 12th, more than 1,000 male and female refugees from Henan arrived in Nantong on seven working boats. Suddenly, they encountered a gale and the boats capsized. Fortunately, it was in shallow water and only more than 20 people drowned. They were rescued by nearby villagers and temporarily sheltered in the port.

Yunzhen's Sand-carrying Ship Carrying American Wheat Went Missing in the Wind: The first batch of American wheat for disaster relief in northern Jiangsu arrived in Nantong. Seven sand-carrying ships were unloaded at Hong Kong and loaded for transportation to the lower reaches of the river. At 1:00 a.m. on the 12th, they were blown away by a strong wind and their whereabouts are unknown.

Yangzhou

Two Bandits Shot After Kidnapping: In May of this year, there was a case of kidnapping the young son of Zhu Zhengke in Youfangqiao for a large ransom. Zhu Zhenggang, one of those previously captured, was sentenced to death and executed by firing squad. The accomplices in this case, Li Dajiao, Yang Yougeng, etc., confessed that Wang Xiaomaozi and He Jianan were both present at the handover of the ransom note and the ransom money and that they all shared the money. Wang and He have now been captured in Taicang County. Police officers were immediately dispatched to escort them to Yangzhou. According to Wang Xiaomaozi's confession, in the case of Zhu Zhengke's family, he negotiated and delivered the ransom note, and he was indeed present at the sharing of the money. In October of last year, they robbed five shops in the Taoist temple in Yangzhou County. In March of this year, they robbed the house of Li Delin in Yongzhou, Taixing. They also robbed Jiang ships at Wujiaqiao and Shenjiatang in Renjiang, and all shared the loot. He has a box cannon with 22 bullets stored elsewhere. According to He Jianan's confession, in the case of Zhu Zhengke's family, they obtained money by kidnapping and extorting a ransom note, which is the same as Wang Xiaomaozi's confession. He also robbed Li Delin's house in Taixing and shared the loot, which he frankly admitted. After recording their confessions, they were telegraphed to the provincial government for approval of the death penalty. Wang and He were taken to the execution ground on the morning of the 11th at 7:00 a.m., where their identities were verified and they were shot by firing squad.

Escapees from the Vagrant Skills Training Center: The National Group of the Jiaxing County Vagrant Skills Training Center discovered that Li Shoukang and Ma Yunsheng had dug up the floor and walls and escaped in the middle of the night a few days ago. After realizing this, they immediately ordered the police to pursue them, but they have disappeared. The director of the center has now reported the case to the county and requested their arrest.

Anqing

Anhui University Students Voluntarily Go to Beijing to Petition

Li Dachang and other students from Anhui University, a provincial university in Anqing, initiated a petition to the capital due to students from various regions going to Beijing to petition. Their patriotic zeal did not want to lag behind others. They initiated the petition to Beijing some days ago, and more than two hundred people signed up willing to go. Thus, on the evening of the 10th, it was decided that they would voluntarily go to Beijing to petition and requested Principal He Lu of the university to return their library deposit as travel expenses. He Lu then submitted this to the tenth administrative meeting of the university, which decided to first dissuade them. If that proved ineffective, the principal should convene a meeting to instruct the petitioning students to strictly maintain order and not betray the essence of patriotism. For the students remaining at the school, from that day until the 17th, in addition to intensifying military training, the regular courses would be temporarily changed to special lectures for two hours each day. Currently, the dissuasion of the students has been ineffective, and they originally planned to depart last night (the 11th). However, due to the lack of a steamer to Anhui, they were unable to proceed. It was decided that they would set off tonight (the 12th). The university has temporarily suspended classes since the afternoon of the 11th.

Page 10

Educational News

Special Article

Socialization of Universities by Gao Jiansi

The issue of schools becoming "centers of society" arose in the United States about twenty years ago. People have both spiritual and material needs. How to satisfy and guide these needs is the sole responsibility of the university. Lecturing, studying, learning, investigating, researching, experimenting, etc., are all methods. Satisfying and guiding the needs of life is the purpose. Methods and purpose are closely related—not only should they not be separate, but they should also be suitable. Methods must be able to achieve the purpose to be considered suitable. For example, good health is the goal, and studying hygiene is the method. If the hygiene being studied does not contribute to good health or even harms it, the irrelevance or unsuitability of the method and purpose is self-evident.

Universities are responsible for satisfying the proper needs of life and guiding improper needs back to the proper path. How can universities fulfill this responsibility? They must be socialized as "centers of society." What is socialization? A university that takes the safety and progress of society as its responsibility is a socialized university. The ancients said, "Everyone is responsible for the rise and fall of the nation," meaning that individuals must be socialized. What we are now clearly advocating is: "The university is responsible for the safety (and progress or lack thereof) of society."

Is not the university the highest institution of learning? Is it not where various experts and social leaders come from? Is it not where the public's expectations lie? University, university, can you not take the safety of society as your responsibility?

Therefore, the instability of world peace, the economic panic, the increasing number of unemployed, the diversion of thought, and China's continuous internal strife, bandits everywhere, backward production, floods, the grabbing of profits and power, the lack of clarity in politics, the decline in customs, and all other kinds of evils—none of these are not due to universities failing to fulfill their duties. From another perspective, the university itself must take responsibility and say, "Do we want lasting world peace? Do we want to reduce unemployment? Do we want China's production to develop? Do we want someone to control the floods? Do we want clear politics?… We must rely on universities, and we must hope for the emergence of university talents." If the university takes on such a responsibility without shirking it, shouldn't studying be socialized?

The socialization of universities can be divided into small and large scales. If a university strives to be the center of a village or town, it can be called a university of that village or town. If it strives to be the center of a country or the world, it can be called a university of that country or the world.

The ancients said, "Everyone is responsible for the rise and fall of the nation." This is to socialize the individual. Today, we say, "The university is responsible for the safety of society." This is to socialize the university. Strive, strive, university socialization!

Important News

Fujian Education Department Initiates National Salvation Savings

(Fuzhou Correspondence) Cheng Shih-Kuei, the director of Fujian Education Department, convened representatives of the academic community to discuss methods for initiating national salvation savings. On the afternoon of the 4th, he convened more than one hundred people, including department heads, faculty members, student representatives, and personnel from social education institutions, for a meeting in the main auditorium. The meeting was chaired by Cheng, who announced three points of significance: (1) National salvation should be based on practical preparation. (2) National salvation savings is a duty that citizens should fulfill. (3) The academic community initiates national salvation savings to promote it in society. Next, they discussed: 1. The principle proposal for national salvation savings, which was approved unanimously. 2. The methods for national salvation savings, which were approved with amendments. The following is an excerpt from the methods for collecting national salvation savings in the academic community of Fujian Province: (1) This savings fund is donated by personnel from educational administrative agencies, faculty and staff of schools, students, and staff of social education institutions in this province. (2) The funds are collected by the donating agencies and submitted to the Central Bank of China or the Bank of China in this province for storage as reserve funds, and a report is made to the Fujian Education Department. (3) Those among the personnel of educational administrative agencies, faculty and staff of schools, and staff and students of social education institutions who donate more than the following standards will be awarded medals by the Fujian Education Department to encourage them. A. For faculty and staff of educational agencies and schools with a salary of less than 100 yuan, a donation exceeding 10 yuan; for those with a salary of more than 100 yuan, a donation exceeding 20 yuan; for those with a salary of more than 200 yuan or 300 yuan, a donation exceeding 30 yuan. B. For students, a donation exceeding 5 yuan. (4) The Fujian Education Department prints three-part receipts, which are given to the bank. When the savings are received, the bank fills them out, delivers the corresponding parts to the depositing agency, and sends one part to the Education Department, with the remaining part kept in the bank for future reference. (5) The deadline for depositing this savings fund into the bank is the end of February of the 20th year of the Republic of China at the latest. (6) Three to five supervisors are stationed at the location where the savings fund is deposited. When withdrawing the savings, the approval of the Fujian Education Department is required, and all supervisors in that location must sign and stamp the document before it can be withdrawn. If the supervisors have not been selected and there is an urgent need for national salvation, the Education Department is responsible for stamping the document and transferring the funds for use. (7) This savings fund is reserved for national salvation needs. If a foreign war occurs, the funds will be remitted immediately. If there is no need to spend them, they should be retained as an educational fund for the province, and the methods will be determined separately. (8) The names of the donors and the amount of savings in each educational institution will be published by the Fujian Education Department in the Education Weekly from time to time, and the total amount of savings and annual interest will be listed and announced by the Education Department.

Nanjing Middle School Students Petition to Return to School

Satisfied with the Reply from the Jiangsu Education Department

Faculty and Staff Refuse to Resume Classes Due to Unresolved School Affairs Issues

Students from the preparatory Jiangsu Provincial Nanjing Middle School, due to the issue of teacher resignations, sent about seventy or eighty representatives to Zhenjiang yesterday to petition. At about four o'clock, they went directly to the Education Department from the train station. Director Chen first sent Section Chief Nie to inquire about the students' intentions, which were stated in four points: (1) Please approve Principal Zhang's resignation. (2) Order faculty and staff to resume classes. (3) Please do not start the vacation early. (4) Please appoint a capable principal. Later, Director Chen himself went to the main auditorium to meet with the students and explained each point of the students' petition: (1) Principal Zhang has worked hard to maintain school affairs for two years. This time, he was persuaded to stay in his position. (2) The faculty and staff stated to the department that the students were not attending classes, so there were no classes for the faculty and staff to teach. If the students are willing to attend classes, the department can urge the faculty and staff to resume teaching as usual. (3) There is no such thing as starting the vacation early. (4) This is related to the first point and does not need to be answered. He also repeatedly advised the students that the patriotic movement should not abandon their studies. This lasted for three or four hours. The students expressed dissatisfaction with the point of retaining the principal and insisted on approving his resignation. Director Chen explained repeatedly, but to no avail. The students said that no matter what, there must be a complete solution. Otherwise, not only will the students coming to the province not be able to return to Beijing, but more than a thousand students in Beijing have also decided to come to the province tomorrow. Director Chen had no choice but to withdraw. Later, Secretary-General Jin of the Provincial Government, upon hearing the news, went to the department and repeatedly persuaded and explained to the students. The students insisted that they were entrusted by the assembly and would not leave the province until the Provincial Government approved Zhang's resignation. Until about one o'clock in the middle of the night, the students still held on in the biting cold. Secretary-General Jin then used a long-distance phone call to ask Chairman, who was in the two capitals, to allow the issue to be submitted to the Provincial Government for resolution. The students then expressed satisfaction. However, as it was already late at night and there was no place to stay, the Education Department could not even arrange for blankets. They huddled around the stove in the main auditorium and talked until dawn, and then took the Beijing-Shanghai train back to Beijing.

Nanjing, 14th Telegraph. The seventy student representatives from Nanjing Middle School who went to Zhenjiang to petition have returned to Beijing and spoke with the faculty and staff representatives, hoping that classes would resume immediately. The faculty and staff said that they would not resume teaching until the principal's issue was resolved.

President Yang of Qingdao University Resigns

Qingdao University President Yang Zhensheng's resignation telegram reads: "Respectfully to Minister Li of the Ministry of Education, Nanjing. One hundred and seventy-nine students of this school have signed up to go to Beijing to petition for anti-Japanese affairs. Despite repeated persuasion, all efforts have been ineffective. When they were about to leave, they jointly asked for leave, but without approval, they left the school on the second of this month. This has been telegraphed. This action, according to the Ministry's orders and school regulations, is unpermitted. However, their actions are driven by patriotic zeal. If punished, the youth's patriotic spirit may be frustrated. If not punished, the school's discipline will not be strict, and there will be no way to maintain it. Zhensheng, holding the position of president of this school, has no other way to handle it than to respectfully request approval to resign, in order to emphasize responsibility and maintain discipline. This is the best course of action."

Local News

Aurora University Experiences Turmoil

Announces Vacation...Students Leave School

Aurora University students decided on the 12th at the University Anti-Japanese Joint Conference that one-third of the students from each school should participate in the demonstration in Beijing. The school's representatives returned to the school that evening. At eight o'clock the next morning, they announced the resolution to all students and convened an emergency representative meeting. It was unanimously decided to comply with the resolution of the joint conference and immediately requested the school's permission. However, the request was rejected three times. At that time, a list of more than one hundred students who voluntarily signed up to demonstrate in Beijing was received. The representative meeting ordered the more than one hundred students who volunteered to participate to prepare everything and decided to hold a plenary meeting during the morning exercise the next day (yesterday morning) and then automatically depart as a whole. The representative meeting itself went to the office to prepare everything.

While the entire representative body of the Anti-Japanese Association was engaged in various matters related to going to Beijing in the office, the dean of academic affairs suddenly led armed police into the room, forcibly removed the representatives from the office, and confiscated all seals and documents. Subsequently, the representatives held a meeting outside the school to respond and decided not to make any announcements that night and to go to the North Station for a demonstration during the military exercise the next day. However, this news was known to students who had a history with the school, who reported it to the authorities. The school immediately announced the start of the New Year vacation that evening and patrolled the school with plainclothes detectives, causing key members of the representative body to not dare stay in the school overnight. Late into the night, the authorities were still using electric torches to patrol each dormitory.

Yesterday, the school ordered everyone except Catholics to leave the school today, and plainclothes detectives patrolled the school, allowing only exits and no entries. Because the key representatives did not dare to return to the school, the students did not know what to do. They could only pack their luggage and leave the school gate. Most of the students had not yet received remittances, and they were being urged to pay for food and miscellaneous expenses they owed, and they were being blocked by creditors at the school gate, leaving them unable to move forward or backward. Afterwards, it was reported that the Anti-Japanese Representative Association of the school decided to register the students, urge them to leave the school permanently, and send all representatives to the Ministry of Education to petition for the return of Aurora's educational rights and to request the establishment of another school to accommodate all the students who left the school.
