Hou Dachun Not Prosecuted

Court Investigation Concluded

The case of Feng Yixian suing Hou Dachun has been investigated four times by the Shanghai District Court Prosecutor's Office. The parties and witnesses have been summoned to court for questioning. The investigation has now concluded, and it has been determined that Hou Dachun has no criminal suspicion and will not be prosecuted.

Chopping Off a Child's Head to Pray for a Dream

Sleeping with the Head as a Pillow Showing No Unusual Signs

How Cruel These "Dahua Hui" Members Are

Near the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway beside the Hanqiao Bridge on Xinmin Road in Zhabei, a man, about thirty years old, was seen carrying a sack and wandering near the tracks at around 6:00 PM last night. After about a few minutes, he threw the sack on the ground and quickly left. The patrol officer there, seeing his suspicious behavior, went forward to investigate and found a child's head inside the sack, which shocked him. He immediately chased after and apprehended the man, taking him to the First Detachment of the Railway Police for interrogation. It was learned that the man's name was Zhu Agou, from Ningbo, and he was a carpenter at the Qiu Guiji Woodworking Shop in Xie Xingli, Gonghe Xin Road, Zhabei. He said that the child's head was used to pray for dreams in the "Dahua Hui." According to his statement, he found a boy's body, about six or seven years old, near the tap water pavilion in Longtoufang, North Station, the day before yesterday. He chopped off the head with an ax in the middle of the night, put it in a sack, and spent the night in a small alley sleeping with the child's corpse as a pillow to pray for a dream. However, he saw nothing unusual, so he sent it back to its original location at about 11:00 AM yesterday, which led to its discovery by the patrol officer. The police are concerned that there may be other motives and will refer him to the court for a thorough investigation.

The Case of the Nephew Killing His Uncle and Two Others is Solved

The Murderer Fled to Wuxi

Entrusted Someone to Come to Shanghai to Withdraw Money

The Bank Reported the Arrest and Solved the Case

The Murderer Was Arrested in Wuxi

Wang Jiashun, the owner of Wang Yuanxing Roundwood Shop at No. 1673 Chexi Road, was asleep in the front building with his wife, Zhang, and son, Xingbao, at midnight on the 5th of this month. Suddenly, his nephew, Wang Songfa, sneaked into the bedroom, murdered for money, and hacked Wang Jiashun, his wife, and Xingbao to death with an ax. He stole more than one hundred dollars in cash and a savings account book from the Siming Bank and fled. The Special Court interrogated the case and ordered the police to strictly arrest and bring the murderer to justice, and notified the Siming Bank to stop payment and pay attention to all information. News of this was published in this newspaper. It is now learned that the case was solved by the Huishan Police yesterday. The murderer and suspects have been arrested in Shanghai and Wuxi. Now, the details of the case's solution are recorded below. After the incident, the murderer, Wang Songfa, fled with the bank book. He then, on the previous week,

To Wuxi Zhoushan Port, He stayed temporarily with his friend Feng Song’s family, but Feng was not rich either, so he had to find a way to maintain his livelihood. Wang Songfa took out a savings account book from the Siming Bank and entrusted Feng to go to Shanghai to withdraw the deposit. But Feng did not dare to go alone rashly, so he went with Xie Jinbao, a native of Jiangyin, to Shanghai on the 12th of this month. They stayed overnight in a small inn near the North Station. On the morning of the next day, Feng and Xie went

Together to the Siming Bank to Withdraw the Money. Xie waited outside the door, while Feng entered alone, took out the bank book and handed it to the clerk. The clerk recognized that the book belonged to Wang Jiashun, and secretly reported it to the Huishan Police. Detective Liu Baoshan was dispatched to arrest Feng and bring the book to the police station. Under questioning, it was learned that his accomplice Xie Jinbao was waiting at the entrance of the Siming Bank, but he may have already taken a train to Wuxi. Chinese and Western detectives immediately took a car to the North Station, where they saw Xie

Buying Tickets. They arrested him and took him to the police station. At the same time, they immediately dispatched detectives, along with Feng Song, to take a train to Wuxi to arrest the murderer Wang Songfa and bring him to justice. Yesterday morning at 9:30, the police sent Xie Jinbao to the First Special District Court to Judge Gao Yi, who, according to the police lawyer Zhang Tianyin, stated that the police had just received a long-distance call from the detectives who had been dispatched to Wuxi to arrest the murderer Wang Songfa, stating that the murderer Wang Songfa had been arrested and would be brought to Shanghai at 11:00 this morning. Therefore, the two criminals Feng and Wang cannot be brought to trial today and must be interrogated tomorrow. But at the time, the police

If They Had Not Rushed to the North Station,

to Arrest Xie, then Xie might have rushed back to Wuxi to report to Wang, and Wang would have been unable to be arrested. Therefore, he requested that Xie be detained and interrogated together with Feng and Wang. Xie Jinbao confessed that he was 21 years old, a blacksmith in Wuxi, and had known Wang Songfa for many years. The day before yesterday, Wang asked me and Feng to come to Shanghai to withdraw the money he had deposited. When we arrived in Shanghai, Feng Song gave me two dollars and told me to keep watch at the entrance of the bank. If he

There Was Any Danger,

I should quickly return to Wuxi. Later, Feng was indeed arrested, and I rushed to the North Station to return to Wuxi and was arrested while buying tickets. But I did not know that Wang Songfa's deposit was obtained by murdering three people. I beg for your judgment. Judge Xiao Xiefen verified the confession and ordered that Xie Jinbao be temporarily detained.

A Member of the Qichang Zhan Security Guard Kills a Robber

Using a Boundary Stone to Break Down the Door

The Robbers Seize a Handgun

Three Victims Injured

The Dead Robber Resembles a Laborer

The home of a member of the security guard of the Qichang Ji Meiyuan residence in Pudong was suddenly robbed yesterday morning, and one robber was killed on the spot. There was no dereliction of duty. The details of the investigation are recorded below:

Shooting a Robber Dead: Lu Liuzhu, 26 years old, is currently a member of the third team of the Yangjing District Security Guard. He lives at No. 66 Meiyuan Residence. His family is well-off, attracting the covetousness of robbers. At 3:35 yesterday morning, while Mr. Lu was asleep, five robbers, speaking in the accents of Chongming and Jiangbei, climbed over the bamboo fence. They used a boundary stone (about three feet long and five inches square) with a blue cloth strip tied to it to break through the outer and inner doors. Two robbers stood guard outside, and two robbers, each wielding a five-inch-long dagger, broke into the bedroom. One robber first snatched two gold hairpins from Mr. Lu's wife, Jin. At this time, Mr. Lu was awakened and quickly grabbed his self-defense handgun from under his pillow. He jumped out of bed and shouted at the robbers not to move. However, the robbers dared to resist, attempting to seize Mr. Lu's handgun and stabbing at Mr. Lu's left and right hands. In pain, Mr. Lu pulled the trigger and fired four shots in succession, killing one robber on the spot. The remaining robbers, seeing the situation was unfavorable, fled.

Three People Injured: Lu's younger brother, Defu, and his father, Jin Quan, were sleeping in another room. When the robbers broke down the door, they got up and put on their clothes, which was seen by the robbers on guard. Defu's left wrist and back were stabbed in two places. Jin Quan, nearly sixty years old, was beaten with a wooden stick, resulting in a bruised back. Yesterday morning, they and Liu Fu took a rickshaw to Pudong Hospital for treatment. It is reported that the injuries of the three are not serious and are expected to fully recover in about two weeks.

The Appearance of the Dead Robber: It has been found that Meiyuan Residence is about six miles away from the third district and about half a mile away from the first police station of Qichang Zhan. Therefore, the police did not hear anything during the robbery. It was not until dawn that the victim sent someone to the district to report the incident. District Chief Zhang immediately went to inspect the scene and found the dead robber lying at the door, wearing a blue cloth short shirt and pants with a black jacket. His shoes had fallen off. He was about thirty years old and looked like a laborer. In his pocket was a red invitation card (reading "This month, the 23rd of the Gregorian calendar, the 15th of the lunar calendar, is my father's 80th birthday celebration. Li Shihou respectfully bows, place set at Zhuangyuan Restaurant, Pingliang Road, Yangshupu, No. 862 Yaohua Lane.") Next to the corpse were three hats, a dagger, and a candle. An order was issued to the local bailiff to report to the local court for an inspection. The dagger, candle, and red invitation card were taken back to the district for a detailed report to the General Bureau for review.

Court Inspection: After receiving the report, the court commissioned Prosecutor Shen Zhaoming and Clerk Yuan, accompanied by staff, to cross the Huangpu River at 3 p.m. to arrive on the scene. After questioning, no family members of the deceased were present to identify the body. The autopsy revealed a gunshot wound on the left chest of the deceased, with the bullet not having exited. It was determined that the deceased had died from a fatal gunshot wound sustained while alive. An order was issued to take photographs and place the body in a coffin, and the deceased's belongings were taken back to the warehouse for further investigation.

Suspect Detained: Because the name of the dead robber was unknown, District Chief Zhang immediately sent someone to notify Li Shihou at the address on the red invitation card to come to the district for questioning. Li firmly denied issuing the invitation card, and because his statements were ambiguous and suspicious, it was decided to temporarily detain him for further investigation and verification.

The Ring Leader of the Robbery on a Ship that Kidnapped Passengers is Arrested in Shanghai

A Certain Ship from Dongting Mountain Was Robbed

Twenty-three Passengers Were Kidnapped

The Ring Leader Liu Jiesan Hides in Shanghai

Has Been Arrested by the French Concession Police

A certain ship traveling between Shanghai and Suzhou Dongting Mountain was robbed on the 23rd of July in the lunar calendar this year, during which a large gang of robbers kidnapped twenty-three passengers. The local authorities issued an arrest warrant for the robbers. Now, the third detachment of the Jiangsu Water Police in Suzhou has captured a member of the gang, who confessed that the ringleader, Liu Jiesan, also known as Liu Changlin, was hiding in a certain inn in the French Concession of Shanghai. The district chief was immediately informed, and a formal request was sent to Shanghai, and Detective Shi Yuanli was dispatched to Shanghai to cooperate with the French Concession Police to arrest the robber Liu. He was taken to the police station and then escorted to the Second Special Court yesterday. First, the police lawyer Fei Xizhen explained the case, followed by Detective Shi Yuanzhang, who complained about the case and requested permission to transfer Liu back for interrogation.

During interrogation, Liu Jiesan confessed that he was from Xuzhou, 32 years old, and had previously worked in the military. The rest of his testimony was evasive. Judge Luo Renji ordered the defendant to be handed over to the detective to be taken back for interrogation.

Measures to Resolve the Issue of Sealed Japanese Goods

Should Be Negotiated with the Anti-Japanese Association by Local Chambers of Commerce

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday replied to the Tongshan County Chamber of Commerce regarding the resolution of the issue of sealed Japanese goods, stating that local chambers of commerce should negotiate with the Anti-Japanese Association. The letter states: "Upon receiving your telegram of the current month, the 12th, we understand that sealed Japanese goods should be resolved quickly to avoid prolonged delays. Localities share the same sentiment. The Shanghai market is particularly affected. Our association has repeatedly urged the Anti-Japanese Association to discuss and announce a resolution as soon as possible based on the demands of various industries. However, due to the great importance of this matter, the association is still considering it carefully. As for how to dispose of the sealed Japanese goods in various localities as soon as possible, it should be handled through direct negotiation between local commercial organizations and the local Anti-Japanese Associations. Our association is limited by its authority and cannot overstep its bounds. We hope for your understanding."

Postponement of the Japanese Textile Mill Conference

To be Scheduled After Takesue Kaneso Arrives in Shanghai

According to a report in a previous newspaper, Japanese textile mills in Shanghai were scheduled to hold a joint representative conference today (the 15th) to discuss a resolution regarding Takesue Kaneso's telegram urging a temporary suspension of the factory shutdowns. Yesterday, a reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency made a special trip to the Japanese Textile Mills Association in Shanghai to inquire about the above news and the important issues of the conference. According to someone from the association, since the 2nd of this month, the textile mill industry in this city, convened by the president of the Textile Industry Association, Imura, held a joint representative conference. All the representatives of the textile mills in Shanghai, due to excessive losses and inability to maintain operations, unanimously refused to accept the original plan to shorten the work hours by 20% and advocated a temporary complete shutdown to wait for an opportunity. However, factories with strong financial resources, if still willing to continue operations, would be allowed to do so at their convenience. Seeing the firm attitude of the representatives, Imura left Shanghai and returned to Japan on the day after the meeting (the 3rd) to report everything to Takesue Kaneso, the president of the Textile Mills Association in China, in Osaka. Unexpectedly, on the evening of the 11th, this association (as the Japanese refer to themselves) suddenly received an urgent telegram from Osaka from Takesue Kaneso, discouraging the representatives of the mills in this port from deciding to shut down the factories and stating that he had found a proper remedy and would implement his proposal after he arrived in Shanghai from Osaka. However, it is not known what method Takesue Kaneso's so-called proper remedy would employ. After receiving this telegram, this association had the motive to convene a joint conference of representatives of various textile mills in Shanghai. It was originally scheduled to be formally held tomorrow (the 15th), but now a temporary problem has arisen. This conference has to be postponed accordingly. As for when the meeting will be held, it will definitely have to wait until Takesue Kaneso arrives in Shanghai before a decision is made.

Consolidated News of Donations for the Support of Ma Zhanshan

The Hardware Industry Association Remits 2,500 Yuan: The Hardware Industry Association sent a telegram to Ma Zhanshan in Hailun, which read: "Chairman Ma of Hailun, your lone army's resistance against Japan is admired by all. Our industry has raised 2,500 yuan, which has been telegraphed to Harbin through Citibank in Shanghai. It is a small contribution to support the military needs. Please send someone to receive it and reply. Sincerely, the Shanghai Hardware Industry Association." Chairman Ma replied by telegram: "To the Shanghai Hardware Industry Association, your telegram has been received. Thank you for your support and generous donation. The officers and soldiers of the three armies share your heartfelt sentiments. Our government has now moved to Hailun. Your donation has been assigned to be transferred from Harbin. Also reported is Ma Zhanshan's gray, sealed message."

Overseas Chinese Returning from the United States Remit Over 900 Yuan: On the 11th of this month, the President Wilson arrived in Shanghai from New York, USA. A third-class passenger on board claimed that when the ship passed through Japan, they had gone ashore with other passengers and crew members for sightseeing. They found groups of three to five Japanese people holding flags with slogans such as "Occupy the Three Northeastern Provinces" and "Down with the Chinese," joyfully dancing and demonstrating in lines. They were insulted at every turn. We were in the tiger's mouth and dared not resist, so we could only swallow our anger and return to the ship. After the ship departed from Japan, all the passengers were overseas Chinese who had lived in the United States for many years. Living in a civilized country, they had never witnessed such barbaric behavior. They mourned our country's declining politics and increasing foreign insults. Some cried bitterly, and some vowed to resist foreign aggression to the death. Then, crew members Xu Maofang, Ye Qinji, Yu Gui, Yan Zheng, Ye Yan, etc. continued to speak with grief and passion, roughly saying that our country has 3 million soldiers and hundreds of thousands of officers, but only General Ma Zhanshan can kill enemies and resist insults. Now, he has retreated to Hailun due to lack of ammunition and reinforcements. So they initiated a fundraising campaign to support Ma. The crew members took the lead, contributing 706 yuan and 6 jiao, and the passengers contributed 285 yuan and 5 jiao. When they arrived in Shanghai on the 11th, the crew members filled out a remittance form at the Bank of China to telegraph it to General Ma. The bank issued two receipts. The passengers were all third-class passengers, and the crew members were also all third-class crew members. If they could have solicited donations from first and second class, the results would certainly have been more than this, it was said.

The Huasheng Company Employees Donate 130 Yuan: All the staff and workers of Huasheng Printing Company, No. 261 North Henan Road, realizing that General Ma Zhanshan is resisting the Japanese invaders with a lone army, and mindful of the difficulties of the army stationed on the frontier, donated 130 yuan. Yesterday, Wang Keqin, an employee of the company, delivered it to the Bank of China to be remitted to General Ma Zhanshan in Hailun as a token of respect.

Ma Zhanshan Thanks the Municipal Chamber of Commerce by Telegram: The Municipal Chamber of Commerce previously remitted 10,000 yuan to General Ma Zhanshan as a reward. According to a telegram from General Ma Zhanshan in Hailun: "To the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Mr. Wang Xiaolai and gentlemen, your letter has been received. Your donation of 10,000 yuan has been received and acknowledged in the reply telegram on the 28th. Thank you for your support." - Ma Zhanshan, gray seal.

Ma Zhanshan Thanks the Chaozhou Association by Telegram: "To the Chaozhou Association in Shanghai, your telegram has been received. Your generous gift is deeply appreciated. I and my troops express our gratitude. Your donation has been dispatched to be transferred from Harbin." - Ma Zhanshan, gray seal.

Jiangbei Disaster Victims in Severe Cold

Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Relief Association Xinghua Disaster Relief Report

The Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Relief Association is the only relief organization in the country. Throughout history, it has been committed to providing disaster relief for major floods and droughts, feeding the hungry and rescuing the drowning. Its contributions to this year's flood disaster are particularly significant. In all heavily affected areas, the association has established branches to actively carry out relief work. Now, the Xinghua branch of the association reports that the floodwaters have not yet receded, indicating the severity of this flood disaster, which is rare in modern times. In addition to providing emergency relief, it is now continuing to provide winter relief. It was first decided by the association to allocate 50,000 yuan, but due to the severity of the disaster, it was insufficient, so another 50,000 yuan was allocated, totaling 100,000 yuan. Xinghua is divided into six districts. The association, together with the government's disaster relief representatives and local charities in the Jiangsu Relief Association, negotiated to divide up the areas in order to achieve full coverage. The association is responsible for the second district and six villages attached to the first district. Its recent work report is excerpted as follows: (1) The allocated 50,000 yuan for winter relief is not enough. (According to the investigator's report, there were originally 23,036 households in the 17 towns and villages in the second district and six villages attached to the first district. Excluding the current number of displaced households, after strict review, there are at least 10,000 disaster-stricken households. According to the investigator's experience, each household has about five members, including adults and children, meaning there are about 50,000 people. If two small children are counted as one adult, each household has three adults, meaning there are actually more than 30,000 people. It is decided to investigate once and distribute three times, giving two portions of wheat flour and one portion of rice. In the first month, each person will receive half a bag of wheat flour. In the second month, each person will receive 1.2 dou of rice. In the third month, each person will receive half a bag of wheat flour. A total of 3,600 dan of rice is needed, at a price of 12 yuan per dan, totaling 43,200 yuan. A total of 30,000 bags of wheat flour are needed, at a price of 2 yuan per bag, totaling 60,000 yuan. The sum of these two is at least 100,000 yuan. The association has approved an additional allocation of 50,000 yuan as mentioned above.) (2) Recent surveys are more detailed, but there have been no changes, and there is no assistance from other organizations or individuals. (3) The association has identified the names of the towns, villages, and hamlets in the second district and six villages, and the number of original households. The list is attached for your reference. (4) It is best to purchase wheat flour from nearby Taixian County, as previously reported. Rice should also be purchased from neighboring counties. The current price is 12 yuan per dan, but it should be prepared early, as it may increase later. (4) Regarding the work steps, it is instructed to provide more assistance to the elderly, weak, men, and women, and to find ways for the young and strong to work, which is the correct way to do things and is highly admired. We will implement it conscientiously. However, the fields in the county are still under water, from three to four feet in shallow areas to six to seven feet in deep areas. There is no work to be done urgently. This plan will be implemented when the opportunity arises. For this winter relief, it is planned to be carried out for three months, with one distribution per month. After the investigation and issuance of tickets, the first distribution will be made according to the number of tickets. Before the second and third distributions, there will be a supplementary investigation of displaced people returning home and extremely poor disaster victims whose food has run out, and relief tickets will be issued and distributed together. Among the three distributions, one will be rice, which will cost more because the disaster victims have not had rice for a long time, so it is used to adjust their diet. Recently, 100 boxes of sweet potatoes have been issued. Once the association receives them, they will be distributed to replace wheat flour. The distribution of clothes has already been entrusted to the investigators, who will discreetly mark the number of items to be given to men, women, adults, and children on the tickets so that they can be distributed together during the distribution."

The report also stated: "The disaster victims of this flood, in addition to food and clothing, also rely on relief materials to build shelters. According to the association's investigation, there are many villages that used to have one or two hundred households, but due to the impact of the flood, none of the houses in the entire village survived. Other collapsed walls and tilted houses are especially conspicuous. The disaster victims have been living in leaky boats or resting on broken dikes for months. Even if the floodwaters recede, they still have no home to return to. The wind and snow are pressing in, and they have no place to shelter. I am afraid that they will not escape death. The situation is especially tragic. The only relief organization in Xingyi planning for this is the county chamber of commerce, which has prepared tens of thousands of reed mats to help them build shelters when the water recedes, but it can only be given to the urban area, and it cannot do more. The association needs a lot of money and dare not make any claims, and other organizations have not made any preparations, so there is nothing to be done. I dare to offer my opinion, if the association is kind enough to pity them, in addition to giving food and clothing, it can raise funds to purchase large quantities of reed mats to help all the homeless disaster victims in the county." It is reported that the association has approved all the requests of the Xinghua branch. As for the construction of thatched huts, it has been replied that it will be allowed to withdraw funds for the event within the relief funds, so as to avoid the disaster victims being displaced.

Zhu Qinglan Telegraphs the Tragic Situation in the Disaster Area

Zhu Qinglan went to Wuhan to investigate the disaster. A telegram came from Wuhan on New Year's Day, stating that there was a strong wind in Hankou on the evening of the 11th, the weather suddenly turned cold, and it froze. On the morning of the 12th, he inspected the Heshan disaster fence. The area is divided into 17 reed fences, with 17,000 disaster-stricken households, totaling 106,076 people, mostly from Mianyang, Jichuan, Tianmen, and Qianjiang. Within a dozen miles, all that could be heard was the sound of hunger and cold. Within an hour, I personally saw several deaths. Then, I went to the Qiaokou disaster fence to inspect, with more than 10,000 disaster victims. The situation was the same. In total, more than 170,000 people have been taken in in the three towns of Wuhan. The number of those who have not been taken in is still unknown. It is said that the number of disaster victims under other names is far from the original need for wheat, cotton, and clothing. This morning, I took advantage of Cai's inspection of the porridge factory and distributed flour in Heshan. He went to Hunan in October to investigate the disaster.

Jiangnan Seawall Aftermath Committee

The seawalls in Baoshan, Taicang, Changshu, and Songjiang counties were impacted by storms, heavy rains, and giant tides in mid-August of this year, and the seawalls were in danger of collapse. Fortunately, the Jiangnan Seawall Engineering Office carried out emergency rescue operations in sections, ensuring safety and preventing unexpected disasters. People from Bintai Changsong County believe that the aftermath of the seawall is unthinkable and have repeatedly telegraphed the Jiangsu Provincial Government, the Department of Civil Affairs, and the Department of Finance, requesting the swift allocation of huge funds to rush the construction of the seawalls in each county as soon as possible to protect the lives of the people. However, due to the huge amount of funds required for the seawall construction, there has been no solution. It is now learned that the authorities have decided to organize a Seawall Aftermath Committee to deal with the aftermath of the seawall as soon as possible. The Jiangsu Provincial Government will allocate 3.5 million yuan as expenses. The candidates for the aftermath committee will be the Jiangsu Provincial Government Construction Department, the Shanghai Municipal Government Public Works Bureau, the Bintai Changsong County Government, the Construction Bureau Director, etc. as ex officio members, and local well-reputed and impartial gentry will be hired as members. The organization will be launched soon.

Retrial Verdict in the Case of the Qinglian Pavilion Owner Accused by His Concubine

Original Verdict Upheld, Both Parties Innocent

Sun Yunqing, the owner of the Qinglian Pavilion market, was previously sued for assault by his concubine Jiang Cuiling in the First Special District Court. The initial trial found Sun Yunqing innocent. Sun countersued Jiang Cuiling for false accusation, and she was also found innocent at the same time. Both parties were dissatisfied with the verdict and appealed to the collegial panel of the Special Court. As a result, Sun was sentenced to a fine of 50 yuan, and Jiang was found innocent. After the verdict, Sun filed a third appeal to the Second Branch of the High Court. The High Court ruled to revoke the original verdict and send it back to the Special Court for retrial, as previously reported in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, the retrial verdict was announced. Sun Yunqing was absent due to illness, and his agent, lawyer Ni Zhengxue, was present in court to await the verdict. Zhou Hanting, the presiding judge, along with assessors Feng and Shen, took their seats in the First Criminal Court and announced the main text of the judgment: Both appeals are dismissed, and the original verdict of the first instance is upheld, both parties are innocent.

Further Hearing of the Housheng Yarn Factory Lawsuit

The directors of Housheng Ziji Yarn Factory, Bei Runsheng, Xue Gansheng (the eldest son of the late Xue Baorun), Fu Hongshui, Zhao Jixiang, Zhang Lanping, Cheng Houkun, and the manager Li Dixian, etc., were previously sued in a criminal case by the factory's employee representatives Jiang Zhonghe, Zhou Qichang, etc., who hired lawyers Tao Wuzhi and Wang Xiubo to file a complaint with the First Special District Court, accusing them of embezzlement of dividends, etc. At the last court hearing, Xue and Fu were absent. The court ordered the five people who were present, including Bei Runsheng, to each provide a guarantor who would ensure their presence at any time for questioning, as previously reported in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, the hearing continued. Because there were many cases, it was already after 5 o'clock when this case was opened. The defendant's agent, lawyer Wu Linkun, stated that the five defendants who were present at the last hearing were all present today, and Fu Hongshui had also rushed back from another place to turn himself in. However, Xue Gansheng was indeed suffering from a severe illness with swelling all over his body, so he was still unable to be present. If the court did not believe this, it could send a forensic doctor to Xue's home at No. 832 Avenue Joffre in the French Concession to investigate, etc. Fu Hongshui then stated that the two of them had been managers at Zhikangzhuang on Tianjin Road. Housheng Yarn Factory had a total of seven shareholders, and he was a shareholder and director with 50 shares. The chairman of the board was the late Xue Baorun. Now, the Housheng Factory has been closed due to losses and has been transferred to the Shenxin Yarn Factory. The presiding judge, Feng Shide, asked Fu whether the Housheng Factory had profits in 1926, 1927, and 1928. Fu answered that there were profits of over 100,000, but after deducting the depreciation fund of 50,000 each year, there was little profit left. He was asked whether the profits had been distributed. Fu answered that because there was only over 10,000 yuan, it was kept in the account. By the second half of 1929, there were losses and the factory was closed. The plaintiff Jiang Zhonghe was then questioned by Judge Feng about how much the Housheng Factory had actually earned in the three years. Jiang answered that, including the so-called reserve fund of 300,000 by the defendant, and according to the manager's report, it was over 900,000. In these three years, there were a total of over 500,000 earned. Because in 1926 and 1927, over 110,000 was earned, and in 1928, over 140,000 was earned, plus the reserve fund of 300,000, the total was 550,000. Moreover, the red accounts also clearly stated how much the net profit was, so depreciation, etc., had naturally already been deducted. Lawyer Wu then presented a flow account book, pointing out that the source of the 300,000 was not a dividend from profits. Therefore, to understand the situation of this case, it was necessary to have an accountant thoroughly investigate all the account books of Housheng. Finally, the plaintiff's lawyer stated that Xue Gansheng, one of the defendants, was the son of Xue Baorun. Now he claimed to be ill, but the truth was unknown. Because Xue Baorun was a major shareholder of the Housheng Factory, holding 55% of the factory's shares. Now that Xue had passed away, his eldest son, Xue Gansheng, was most familiar with the affairs of the factory and was a key figure in this case. He must be present. Please arrest him or order him to provide bail. Judge Feng reported this and, as it was already 7 o'clock, ordered that the case be adjourned pending the appointment of an accountant to audit the accounts, and that another hearing be scheduled. Fu Hongshui was ordered to provide a guarantor who would ensure his presence at any time. The remaining people were each ordered to provide their original guarantors. A forensic doctor was also sent to Xue Gansheng's home to investigate and verify the situation.

Reader Correspondence

Mr. Wang Yongkang Entrusts a Message to Mr. Liu Xintao

(Discussing the Establishment of a Porcelain Company)

Mr. Xintao, after reading your article in Shenbao, "A Brief Description of Porcelain Making in Jingdezhen," I know that you are an enthusiastic advocate of national products and that you are very knowledgeable about the porcelain industry. Since we and our colleagues left school in 1925, we have witnessed the decline of domestic industry and frequent foreign insults. Therefore, we have united with our comrades to promote national products. Also, in view of the fact that Jingdezhen porcelain is a famous product of our country, we established the Jingdezhen Porcelain Company on Nanjing Road and sent Mr. Tan to Jingdezhen to investigate the porcelain industry, hoping to improve it in the future. However, in recent years, although we have worked hard, the only results we have obtained are being bullied and sabotaged by colleagues who stick to conventions. There has been no benefit to the porcelain industry itself. We feel ashamed when we examine ourselves at night. Now, after reading the newspaper, we all express sympathy for your enthusiasm. Therefore, we intend to make you a comrade. In the future, we hope that you will teach us about all the aspects of the porcelain industry that should be promoted and reformed. If you intend to launch a kiln company or a porcelain factory, we would be happy to sponsor it and do our best to promote national products. We would be very grateful if you could inform us of the organizational outline and plan.

Mr. Chang's Message (Discussing Electrical Porcelain Industry with Mr. Liu)

Having read Mr. Liu Xintao's description of porcelain-making in Jingdezhen published in this column on December 11, due to my shared interests, I dare to consult with Mr. Liu, though I am a humble man. In my opinion, porcelain-making is an important type of ceramic industry, which is on par with glass, enamel, and brick industries. Each of the western and eastern countries has numerous factories, and universities establish specialized studies of these industries which are as important as electronics, mechanics, civil engineering, etc., thus becoming extremely developed. On the other hand, looking back to China, despite being the first country to invent porcelain, the modern factories have remained lacking, and research and experiments are even rarer, which is a pity. Given such an environment, if one wishes to gather capital of tens of thousands or millions of yuan to establish a factory for manufacturing, I am afraid it is not easy to gain the trust of entrepreneurs. Even if we only gather tens of thousands of yuan to first conduct trial runs, we need entrepreneurs with far-sighted vision willing to sacrifice, in my opinion, it would be better to collect fund from 50,000 to 100,000 to manufacture electrical porcelain, and set up research and improvement for the daily necessities to prepare for future expansion. This is because electrical porcelain (referred to as "electrical porcelain") is easier to manufacture, and doesn’t require much research. Yizhong Company and Qixin Company in Tangshan are both engaged in this industry and have done so for several years. As for the larger scale factories, there are also plants established by foreigners in Shanghai, with more than ten years of history. All equipment and manufacturing methods are new. Because manufacturing daily necessities such as cups and saucers are roughly similar, they have also tried to manufacture these, and have seen good results. However, since there are no experienced workers as in Jingdezhen, and electrical porcelain is not their focus, they have not developed this. Only manufacturing electrical porcelain is guaranteed to be problem-free. This way of production, while doing research, will surely gain the support of all parties. As for the location of the factory, I agree with Mr. Liu's high opinion that Hukou is a great location. But in the first phase of experiments, it is still better to be in Shanghai. There are all kinds of conveniences, and when the trial results are in and a large-scale effort will be required, then factories can be established inland. Regarding the matter of talents, Mr. Liu's opinion of sending students to study abroad is also the most important step. It is best to establish a ceramic studies department in the national universities to train talents, so that there won't be a lack of talent in the future, and it is possible to see the revitalization of the porcelain industry. Regarding the porcelain industry, it includes daily necessities (such as cups, bowls, dishes, teapots, etc.), decorations, bathroom utensils, electrical and chemical products. In addition, the manufacture of floor tiles and wall tiles is similar. The amount of foreign goods imported into our country every year is countless, and electrical porcelain is almost entirely Japanese goods. This is because although the quality is inferior, the price is low. During the current time of resistance, it is a great opportunity for entrepreneurs to invest. I am willing to discuss this with my fellow countrymen.

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast for 4:30 PM yesterday was as follows: The Shandong coast and the Yangtze River basin will be cloudy and unsettled, with occasional fog in some areas. The area south of Ma'anshan Island will be sunny. Along the coast north of Taiwan, the winds will be gentle and unsettled. There will be strong northeasterly winds in the Taiwan Strait. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the temperature in this city was a maximum of 48.3 and a minimum of 21.2. On the same day last year, the maximum was 52.7 and the minimum was 34.9.

Shanghai Market

Market News

Wing On Company declares that the cosmetic department has received a large number of gift cosmetics and fragrances from famous French factories, with more than 10,000 items in total, in all colors and beautifully decorated. Among the various new fragrances that have arrived, the most distinctive is the Love Flower fragrance from the famous Parisian D'orsay factory, which is the most precious and each set is priced at 375 yuan. According to the manager of the factory, this kind of high-end fragrance has never arrived in Asian ports, and this is the first time it has come to Shanghai.

Sanyanglou, south of Tianfei Palace Bridge, declares that every winter, the building is bound to order grass carp from Huzhou, and high-level chefs are invited to cook the head and tail of the grass carp, not only is the taste delicious, but also fat and palatable. This is because the grass carp produced in Huzhou is different from those produced in the Yangtze River. The building does not hesitate to make sacrifices, and orders daily from the Huzhou liner ships, to meet the needs of customers. In addition, the dumplings made by this building are purely Huizhou-style and sold in large quantities every day, and have a monopoly of the market.

Theater News

New Guangda Theater declares that "The Broken Bridge Remnant Dream" was originally a masterpiece of the American drama world. Now it has been adapted into a movie, and it is even more unprecedented. The plot is poignant, warm, and magnificent, and the descriptions are profound, delicate, graceful, and superior. The leading actress is the incomparably poignant superstar Marlene Dietrich, so the performance is very brilliant. It is now playing at the New Guangda Theater, and the audience has been exceptionally crowded in recent days.

Publishing News

Wuxi Provincial Education Institute declares that the third issue of the third volume of Education and the Masses, published by the institute, has been published, with more pages and more content. Important works include Dr. Reinan's Two Cases of Doubt in Modern Chinese Education, Dr. Chen Lijiang's Economic View of Public Education, Du Dingyou's Problems in the Arrangement of Public Dictionaries, and Xiang Yihua's Abstract of Important Works on Worker Education. There are also many original works. It is a magazine that those engaged in public education and research on public education must read. In addition, this journal is now sold to a wide range of people and has a great impact on the public education cause. It publishes and solicits as much publicity as possible for public education books and various agricultural tools, so that those who run public education and improve agricultural tools in various places know what to buy. Chen Dabai of the institute has been specially assigned to Shanghai to discuss advertising matters. It has been negotiated that the Commercial Press's textbooks for public schools, the Shijian Tongyi Hall's supplies for public education halls, the Chinese Chess Company's various educational toys, as well as Rixin Yudi Publishing House, Dalong Iron Factory, Zhonghua Iron Factory, Datong Bookstore, and World Bookstore, etc., also publish many advertisements, so the content is becoming more and more substantial.

Social News

The Economic Recession in the Dutch East Indies by Qiu Bin Cun

(I)

The Dutch East Indies, encompassing 734,000 square miles, is sixty times the size of the Netherlands itself. The importance of the Dutch relationship with its East Indies colony is akin to the vital connection of the British Empire to its Indian colony.

The production of the Dutch East Indies holds a significant position in the international market. Its main products include quinine, accounting for 90% of world production; kapok, 80%; pepper, 70%; rubber, 30%; tin and tea, both 20%; and cane sugar and coffee, both 10%.

Amidst the current global economic downturn, the economy of the Dutch East Indies is naturally experiencing a major blow. The prices of its main products have plummeted. For instance, the market price of rubber per picul (担) has fallen from 280 guilders to 18 guilders; the market price of cane sugar per picul has dropped from 18 guilders to 8 guilders; and the market price of pepper per picul has decreased from 180 guilders to 50 guilders. The prices of other products have also experienced significant reductions.

Affected by the global economic panic, the Dutch East Indies inevitably suffers from the chronic disease of commercial recession. This recession naturally leads to the following phenomena in society:

(1) Restriction of Production: A single example suffices to illustrate the rest. Take sugar, for instance. Because the Russians, with lower prices than the Java Sugar Trust, adopted a dumping policy, selling at a reduced price in British Malaya, British India, and elsewhere in Southeast Asia, the cane sugar of the Dutch East Indies had no choice but to be sold at a loss. Furthermore, due to Cuba's reduction in cane sugar planting, the Dutch government had to issue an order restricting this year's cane sugar production to 2.4 million tons, a decrease of 500,000 tons compared to last year's 2.9 million tons. It was also stipulated that in the next three years, 100,000 tons could be added each year, reaching 2.7 million tons by 1934, after which this would be the standard production amount.

(2) Merchant Bankruptcies: The Medan Dutch Chamber of Commerce held an officers' meeting to discuss commercial issues. During the meeting, the chairman of the Chamber expressed numerous observations on this year's commercial market, stating that the business slump has been worsening. In the past three quarters, the number of merchants declaring bankruptcy has exceeded 250. Moreover, this number will increase even more in the upcoming quarter, as the end of the year approaches. Therefore, it is estimated that bankruptcies in this semester will not be less than 400. In 1930, there were 175 bankruptcies; in 1929, there were 118; in 1928, there were 81; and in 1926, there were 52. From this, it is evident that the business of this island has been in a decline since 1926. Considering the entire Dutch East Indies, the number of bankruptcies this year is at least in the thousands.

(3) Unemployment: According to a secretary of the Dutch East Indies Commercial Union, speaking to a reporter of the Dutch East Indies newspaper, the union currently has 841 members, of whom 71 are unemployed, meaning one in every ten is unemployed. Previously, female stenographers and typists could easily find positions earning 250 guilders per month, but now, earning 150 guilders per month is considered fortunate.

Furthermore, according to a report released by the Batavia labor exchange on September 17th, as of the end of June this year, the number of unemployed had reached 8,400, including 2,400 Europeans, 460 Chinese, and 5,500 indigenous people. The majority of these unemployed individuals seek secretarial positions, but the local demand is for technicians and those with other specialized knowledge. As for secretarial positions, government offices and shops have long been overstaffed. No wonder the number of unemployed is increasing daily. The majority of the unemployed are secondary and middle school graduates, not counting the uneducated workers.

(4) Sharp Decline in Trade: A large volume of import and export trade in a region indicates a thriving economy. Conversely, a small volume indicates economic decline. Currently, the foreign trade of the Dutch East Indies is simply in sharp decline. Let us examine the comparative table of imports and exports for the years 1928, 1929, and 1930:

Year Imports Exports Total

1928 1030 1590 2620

1929 1166 1488 2654

1930 923 1233 2156

In these three years, exports decreased year by year. Imports only increased in 1929 compared to 1928, but an increase in imports is not a good sign. Moreover, imports decreased significantly again in 1930. Comparing 1930 with 1929, imports decreased by 243 million guilders, exports decreased by 255 million guilders, and the total trade volume decreased by 500 million guilders, which is undoubtedly a substantial amount.

Let us also look at the general situation of imports in Java in September of this year, as released by the Batavia Central Bureau of Statistics. It is reported that imports in September of this year totaled 99,870 tons, valued at 36,458,000 Dutch currency. In the same month last year, imports were 152,239 tons, valued at 50,594,000 Dutch currency. As for the statistics from January to September, this year's total was 1,304,846 tons, valued at 411.809 million Dutch currency, while the same period last year was 1,470,034 tons, valued at 526.376 million Dutch currency. From this, we can understand that the trade of the Dutch East Indies is declining month by month and year by year.

(5) Austerity Measures: Since the economic recession occurred this year, the Dutch East Indies government in Batavia has had to adopt austerity measures to cope with government expenses. The original decision was to approve a 10% salary reduction for all civil servants working in government agencies throughout the Dutch East Indies, starting from January 1st of next year. However, according to the Ministry of Finance's budget, due to the national treasury's deficit, the government suggested to the Dutch government that the date of the salary reduction be moved forward to November. The Governor-General has approved this, and the estimated amount of savings in expenditure for two months is 1.5 million guilders.

(6) Issuance of Public Bonds: In planning to remedy the shortfall in government expenses, the Dutch East Indies government in Batavia, in addition to actively implementing austerity measures of layoffs and salary reductions, has also initiated the issuance of public bonds to compensate. The reasons for and amount of the issuance of public bonds have been submitted to the Dutch East Indies National Council for approval and to the Dutch Colonial Minister for review. The amount of public bonds issued by the Dutch East Indies government is 200 million guilders. This amount exceeds previous issuances in the Dutch East Indies because the current government's income is insufficient to cover its expenses, amounting to a deficit of 53.6 million. Without this remedy, the deficit would further increase to ten to twenty million. Combined with previous debts, the total would be over 200 million guilders. The Dutch government does not consider the issuance of this large public bond to be excessive.

Based on the descriptions in the previous six sections, it can be seen that the economy of the Dutch East Indies is trapped in a dilemma.

(II)

Among those suffering the most from the economic recession in the Dutch East Indies, it is the local masses, not the Dutch East Indies government. The government is hypothetical, not real. Government finances are based on expenditure within income. If government expenses are insufficient, they can still be taken from the masses to make up for the shortfall. Of the total population of 51 million in the Dutch East Indies, indigenous people account for 49 million, Chinese account for 1.2 million, and Dutch people account for only 154,000. Our vast community of 1.2 million Chinese suffers particularly greatly under the economic recession in the Dutch East Indies. I will now provide a brief analysis:

(1) Chinese Merchant Bankruptcies: According to a Batavia dispatch, on September 25th, the Batavia High Court declared 15 Chinese businesses bankrupt. Assuming an average of 15 Chinese bankruptcies per month in Batavia alone, the annual total would be 180. Moreover, considering the Chinese businesses bankrupt in the provinces of West Java, Central Java, East Java, Sumatra, Borneo, Celebes, the Moluccas, and the Lesser Sunda Islands, the annual number of bankrupt businesses would be no less than several thousand.

(2) Repatriation: According to a Medan dispatch, when the ship "Kimma" of the Paketvaart line set sail from Haikou, it was found that 116 Chinese were being repatriated to their hometowns by the local government due to lack of residency rights. In addition, 60 Chinese workers were being repatriated from various plantations of the Deli Maatschappij due to layoffs, totaling 176 people. Assuming that there are at least three or four ships sailing from Medan and Batavia to China each month, and that each time hundreds of Chinese are repatriated or voluntarily return to their homeland due to lack of employment, the total number of Chinese repatriated or voluntarily returning to their homeland each year is at least tens of thousands.

(3) Forced Closures: According to a Singapore dispatch, the Riau Islands, under the rule of the Dutch East Indies government, are lush with forests and abundant in fuel. Consequently, Chinese charcoal merchants in Bengkalis have established hundreds of charcoal kilns on the Riau Islands. However, due to heavy taxation and high costs, coupled with poor business in recent times, businesses are unprofitable. The Dutch East Indies Forest Minister has invoked forest protection as a pretext to order all Chinese charcoal kilns on the islands to close by the end of June. After protests from the Chinese Consuls-General in Singapore and Batavia to the Dutch East Indies government, the Dutch side agreed to consider the situation and execute the closures in stages. Dutch East Indies forest officials and income tax officials have repeatedly met in Bengkalis to discuss the matter. Chinese charcoal merchants, facing the current business slump, have no choice but to voluntarily close their charcoal kilns. Therefore, 50 Chinese charcoal kilns in Riau, Lingga, and Singkep have complied with the order and closed down, incurring losses of at least one million yuan, according to industry insiders. Approximately 10,000 charcoal makers have been laid off, 90% of whom are Malays, with Chinese accounting for only 10%. After being laid off, the Malays mostly switched to fishing, while the Chinese workers had no choice but to return to China. It is reported that the remaining 50 Chinese charcoal kilns have also received notices from the Dutch East Indies government to be closed down separately between the end of this year and June of next year. The losses for the Chinese merchants and the loss of livelihoods for the Chinese and Malay workers will become even more severe.

Other businesses, such as tin mines, rubber plantations, and cane sugar farms owned by Chinese merchants, are also suffering from the same misfortune of being ordered to close, suspend tapping, and restrict production by the Dutch East Indies government. Chinese workers are even more at a loss as to how to find a way out.

(III)

The name "Nanyang Islands" has always been associated with the adjective "golden." From this phrase, we can realize that Nanyang fully embodies the color of gold. Indeed, in the past, Nanyang was filled with the charm of intoxicating people. Our overseas Chinese have also built magnificent palaces in the economy of Nanyang. Therefore, our overseas Chinese have always regarded Nanyang as an "earthly paradise." Nanyang has never understood what a recession is, except after the outbreak of the European War, when some goods could not be imported due to military influences, causing shortages, and some goods could not be exported, causing surpluses, slightly revealing the knot of a recession.

But now, as capitalism has fully developed to the final stage of the third period of financial capital, the economy of the world, especially the economy of industrially advanced nations, has experienced an unprecedented and major recession. The Dutch East Indies is also under the dense clouds of this recession. As a result, goods are restricted from production due to lack of outlets, shops are closed due to lack of business, people lack purchasing power due to loss of employment, tariffs decrease due to the decline in imports and exports, and the government implements austerity measures and issues public bonds to make ends meet due to the shortfall in government expenses. The hardships of the people's livelihood are endless, and our overseas Chinese are clamoring incessantly under these dark clouds. Finally, we can conclude that the golden age of our overseas Chinese in the Dutch East Indies and other places in Nanyang has passed.

The Red River of Batavia by Bin Cun

In Batavia (also called Jakarta or Batavia) in the Dutch East Indies, there is a river called the Red River. The reason why this river is named the Red River is because the overseas Chinese once sacrificed themselves under the iron heel of Dutch imperialism, "their blood flowing into channels," shedding countless amounts of fresh blood, dyeing the river red.

I once went to Batavia at the invitation of a Chinese newspaper there. Friends there told me that during the Qianlong era of the Qing Dynasty, the Dutch colonial government wanted to force our overseas Chinese in the East Indies to pay an exorbitant tax. The overseas Chinese in Batavia, unable to endure the exploitation by the Dutch, became inflamed with national consciousness and opposed it. The Dutch government then ordered troops to massacre the overseas Chinese. The local overseas Chinese gathered to resist, and as a result, tens of thousands of overseas Chinese were brutally killed. Red blood spewed into the sky, and this Red River became the most important page in the history of overseas Chinese in the Dutch East Indies. The Dutch troops had sharp weapons and the government as their backing, naturally taking advantage of their position. Our overseas Chinese, however, had no weapons for combat and no government to support them, naturally destined to fail and harbor hatred without redress.

The Dutch government, realizing that the massacre of the overseas Chinese was too brutal and extensive, became somewhat afraid of starting trouble. Therefore, it sent an envoy to the Qing court to apologize. According to common sense, the Qing court would surely raise a punitive expedition to argue with them. However, the Qing court's response was, "Overseas traitors are not subjects of the Great Qing. Killing them is of no consequence. The court never interferes." The Dutch, receiving such a response, became even more unbridled in their brutal methods of massacre and had no fear.

The overseas Chinese, completely defeated and hopeless, and with the enemy's flames becoming more intense, could not help but develop a terrifying desire for mutual destruction. Therefore, they cut off their fingers, changed their clothes, pretended to be indigenous people, and lived with them to avoid being hunted by the Dutch troops. Over time, they assimilated with the indigenous people and forgot that they were of the Chinese nation. They could not even know their own ancestral origin and surname. Occasionally, when someone asked them, they were at a loss for words. This situation, common in various parts of Java, is truly pitiable. The Dutch massacre of our overseas Chinese is painful, and the Qing court's abandonment of our overseas Chinese is hateful.

Now, the situation in China is different. Our national government under the Party is very concerned about the suffering of overseas Chinese and wants to find solutions. The overseas Chinese in Batavia should know how to unite in spirit and use the Red River formed by our blood to irrigate the blood flowers of the overseas Chinese there, so that Batavia will forever be a paradise for our overseas Chinese immigrants.

Examples of Social News Articles

(1) The text should be about domestic and foreign science, industry, commerce, rural areas (2) Health, aviation, exploration, customs, or urban life, etc., written in each subject related to social life.

(3) Photographs should be about youth life (such as sports, travel, acting, gatherings, exhibitions, various competitions, etc.) school news and youth sports. Both individual and group photos are welcome. Do not write on both sides of the paper.

(4) Each article should not exceed two thousand words.

(5) Write horizontally, do not write carelessly, Western text can be omitted if possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached to the translation.

(6) Do not write the draft horizontally, do not write carelessly, Western text can be omitted if possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached to the translation.

(7) Do not use ink to draw pictures, and do not use colored paper. Use white paper and black ink.

(8) Please specify that the submitted manuscripts are to be sent to the Youth Garden Editorial Department.

(9) Submitted manuscripts will not be returned whether they are published or not. If you need to return them, you should declare in advance and attach a stamped envelope.

(10) The remuneration is divided into three types: three yuan, two yuan, and one yuan per thousand words. The same applies to each picture and photograph. If there are special manuscripts, the remuneration will be calculated separately.

Book Review

"History of Japanese Imperialist Aggression Against China" by Ai Xuan

Written by Jiang Jianren

The lessons of history never deceive. "Do not forget the past, it is a guide for the future." We who are heartbroken by the aggression of the violent Japanese should recognize the historical development of Japan's aggressive policies and carefully and meticulously settle this old score. We must not believe that this Japanese aggression in the Northeast is the ambition of a few warlords, a sudden event. History tells us that this is an inevitable stage in the history of imperialist aggression. In fact, it has recently been fully proven how deliberately the Japanese have planned this incident. The pitiful people of our country have spent their years in a daze. On the day the incident occurred, the whole country was at a loss. "A nation that has forgotten the lessons of history will never have a chance to raise its head." How should we learn from this lesson of history? I am introducing a book to readers as the first step.

The structure of this book is very sound, with systematic and accurate statistics, but it is not a running account. It has faithful and detailed theories, but it does not fall into the empty talk of "accumulating nouns." It has neither very profound and boring academic discussions, nor is it a superficial work that gathers scattered words and compiles them into a chapter. This can be regarded as the only reason why this book is a suitable reading material for the general public. Below, please briefly describe its content and structure.

This book is divided into three parts. The first part describes "The Causes, Policies, Methods, and Periods of Japanese Aggression Against China." This can be said to be the theoretical basis of this book, telling readers why Japan occupies the most chapters in "The History of Imperialist Aggression Against China." The author's opinion is:

1. There are six reasons for Japan's aggression against China: (1) Japan's overpopulation in the past sixty years has forced it to open up territory and emigrate abroad, so it came to China, which is vast and sparsely populated. (2) Because Japan has too little arable land, and the production of rice cannot increase with the population, there is a fear of food shortages, so it invaded our country, which is rich in products. (3) In order to make profits and develop its industry, Japan wanted to take this densely populated and vast China as the only market for its goods. (4) It aims to seize China's raw materials such as coal, iron, soybeans, cotton, and wool. (5) Japan wants to actively invest its surplus capital in China in order to reap the greatest profits. Because of these reasons, Japan "cannot but, to some extent, exploit China's interests, harm Chinese society, and seize Chinese political power," and recently, it has even further annexed Chinese territory.

2. The author lists four policies of Japan's aggression against China: (1) The continental expansion policy, "the purpose of which is entirely to occupy Korea and Manchuria and build a continental empire." The current facts show that the author has unfortunately hit the mark. (2) The maritime expansion policy. (3) The hard-line policy towards China. (4) The soft policy towards China. "Imperialism is a butcher that kills without spilling blood." How can China's weak diplomacy be a match for these insidious methods? "Therefore, if we want China's liberation, we can only use the strength of the Chinese nation itself to exchange it with blood and flesh, and no longer stretch our necks to Geneva or Paris."

3. The methods of Japan's aggression against China: (1) Military oppression. (2) The establishment of politically unequal treaties. (3) Economic aggression. The South Manchuria Railway Company is the commander's platform for Japan's annexation of the Northeast this time. (4) Japan is also very fierce and powerful in cultural aggression, resulting in countless "Japanese obedient citizens" and not a few "Japanized Chinese." (To be continued)
